Machinery Mounts Procedure, Revision I I January 10, 2003
Attached is the revised standard designing and detailing procedure for machinery mounts. Please delete the
contents from Section 2B of your Standard Book II, Volume I and add the attached documents in its place.
Revision 1 Details:
1. This procedure was completely overhauled with the written instructions updated to provide information on
and illustrations of machinery mount configurations and to incorporate and distinguish Pro Engineering and
AutoCAD instructions for creating fabrication drawings.
2. The reference drawings were updated from three drawings into two sets of drawings in order to separate
designing standards (dwgs. 4SDI and 4SD2) from detailing examples (dwgs. 4B and 4C). The two previous
reference drawings for induced draft designs were incorporated into one drawing (4SD2).
3. The BILL OF MATERIAL was deleted on all drawings to eliminate discrepancies with the Standard Book I
procedures pertaining to part description and bill of material placement. Standard Book I procedures are your
primary source for part descriptions and BOMrequirements.
4. Connection holes have been added to the forced draft design shown on drawing 4SD I to reflect the hinge
location of the new fan guards wi hinges.
5. The HPC shop's fit-up holes have been added to 4SDI and 4SD2 drawings per the shop's request. Three
13/16" xl" slots were added to the side channel web and are located 2" from the bottom flange with two
placed near the c-channel stiffeners and one located at fan centerline. Also added was an 11116" xl" slot to
the bottom flange at the fan centerline.
6. The DESIGNING NOTES were revised for the following:
a. The center location for vibration switches is standardized to I' from the fan centerline and 6" from the top
of the machinery mount. Mounting hole dimensions for commonly used vibration switches were tabulated
and added to 4SDI and 4SD2 drawings.
b. The machinery mount length formulas were revised for the two most common conditions.
c. Information pertaining to the diagonal braces was revised and tabulated. The spacing from the c-channel
stiffener to the plan brace will be in even 1/4" increments, with the spacing existing between I" and 6 114'.
If you have any questions or comments contact John Galvan at ext. 8138 or me at ext. 8183.

Issuance of General Arrangement Procedure, Revision 0 July 21,2000
I
Attached is the first issuance of General Arrangement standards. Included in the attached package are the
General Arrangement Procedure, Standard Drawings, and Standard Documents.
The written procedure outlines general arrangement issues such as file maintenance, terminology, wording
and requirements of the GA notes. The standard drawings are designed to illustrate the appropriate
methods for and calculation formulas to enable the designing and detailing of the GA; the standard
documents provide reference information from which GA information is extracted.
Please add the GA procedure to Section I - GA & Assembly of your Standards Book II, Vol. I.
If you have any questions or comments concerning the contents, please contact me at ext. 5873 or the
Standards Department at ext. 5938

SUBJECT:
Engineering Standard Book II Issuance I DATP:ebruary 2, 1999
Standard Book II, Volumes I and II is the fourth of several standards books to be issued. This standard book is
being assigned and issued to you as a source of information regarding work instructions in connection with your
position. You should become familiar with the contents in order that you may perform your duties in strict
compliance with the established work instructions.
The purpose of these standard books is to have an indexed location for current information. Standard Book II is
divided into two volumes. Volume I pertains to GA, Assembly, Mechanical and Panel series subjects, Volume II
pertains to Structural, Frames, and Walkways series subjects, plus miscellaneous subjects. The contents of
Standard Book II include new work instructions and previously issued Engineering & Drafting Procedure
Changes Notices and Drafting Information Notices. Please discard all previous Engineering & Drafting
Procedure Change Notices and Drafting Information Notices that now appear in Standard Book II. Section
Leaders please advise your personnel to not VOID and retain their copies of previously issued information. At
times new information will be issued to update this book by indexing it in the proper place. It is your
responsibility to maintain an up to date standard book.
Also, Standard Book II related information, e.g., notes, sketches, you have but is not included in this issue of
Standard Book II is to be turned over to the Standard Department (John Galvan). Any discrepancies within this
book as well as in the previously issued Standard Books I, III & IV, are be copied, marked-up and turned over to
the Standard Department.
If you have any questions or comments concerning the contents, please contact me at ext. 5873 or the Standards
Department at ext. 5938.
Distribution:

General Arrangement Procedure Revision 1 Oetails:
1. The majority of the revisions were subtle and consisted of expanding existing information. For
example, the terminology section, page 6, has been re-arranged according to HPC and Industry
usage. Also: center columns have been added to the structural illustration on page 12, material
commonly used for bug screens has been added on page 14, the information on reference and
standard drawings has been expanded on page 17, color code information has been added on page
20. The reference documents have been encompassed into the written procedure and Appendix K
now serves as an index of GA standard drawings.
2. The identification notation INLET ENO replaces the use of NOZZLE ENO on the GA drawings.
This is the new standard and is effective on drawings not yet checked.
3. A notation box has been added to drawing 11 SO1. The notes within this box are applicable to all
General Arrangement standard drawings.
4. Primary dimensions are illustrated on drawings 11 SO 1 and 11 S02. Specific dimensions are not
provided onthese drawings because they will be specifictothejob. The Key Plan (11SO1)and
Anchor Bolt Plan (11 S02) drawings are set up as examples and should be used as a guide when
detailing such plans for a job.
5. A table illustrating the maximum fan diameter has been added to drawing I IS03. Also, the GA
notes were removed from this drawing. Information such as note sequence and examples for
completing the notes is located within the written procedure. The AutoCAO block for the GA notes
has been revised to reflect the latest note requirements and is located on the Standards and
Procedure server.
6. Information pertaining to Induced Oraft units has been added to drawing II S04. The additional
illustrations detail parameters to consider in determining plenum and hood height, they highlight
criteria to consider when designing thru-bolt coverplate headers with common column. And, the
illustrations also highlight criteria to consider when designing shaft-thru multi-bundle units. In
addition, formulas for calculating nozzle locations, illustrations of bundle types, and notation
defining the gap between multi-bundles have been added to this drawing.
7. A table listing the three most common platform channels has been added to drawing II S05. Also,
the formula for calculating column distances, location for mechanical walkway, and notation
example for sloped bundles have been added to this drawing.
8. The lifting arrangement illustration has been removed from drawing II S06.
9. The formula for dimensioning walkway between hoods has been added to drawing 11 S07.
10. Information pertaining to the access doors has been added to drawing II S08.
I I. A lifting arrangement illustration for induced draft units has been added to drawing IIS09. Also,
repetitive information has been deleted from this drawing.

GENERAL ARRANGEMENT PROCEDURE
1.0 PURPOSE
1.1 To document infonnation for designing and detailing General Arrangement drawings.
1.2 To define the configuration of most commonly occurring unit components in the General
Arrangement in order to sustain unifonnity and provide consistency in designing and detailing
practices.
1.3 To document the purpose of the General Arrangement drawing which is to provide customers with
infonnation of unit components, as specified by API, in relation to each other and to other units,
and to enable customers to incorporate the unit(s) into their plant layout.
2.0 CONTENTS
1.0 PURPOSE 1
2.0 CONTENTS 1

4.0 ASSOCIATED DOCUMENTS
4.1 The following documents may be affected by General Arrangement changes.
Proposal Drawing
Drawing Schedule
Design/Drafting Checklist
Fin-Fan Specification Sheet
Weight & Weld Metal sheet
Bundle Worksheet
Parts List (during revisions)
Assembly drawings (10 series) (during revisions)
Door drawings (2 series) (during revisions)
Panel drawings (3 and 23 series) (during revisions)
Machinery Mount drawings (4 series) (during revisions)
Structural drawings (5 and 25 series) (during revisions)
Header details (6 series) (during revisions)
Tube and Steam Coil Bundle Frames (7 series) (during revisions)
Walkway details (8 and 28 series) (during revisions)
Louver/Bug Screen drawings (9 and 29 series) (during revisions)
4.2 If the General Arrangement drawing is changed, these documents should also be checked for
changes. Conversely, a change in any of these documents may affect the General Arrangement
drawing(s).
4.3 Within this procedure, the text format COURIER NEW emphasizes a function and/or terminology;
TIMES NEW ROMAN BOLD represents terminology existing or as it will appear on the General
Arrangement. On the Standard Drawings the text format times new roman italicized are
designing and detailing notes referring to sources or formulas.
4.4 The following manuals are to be used for completing the General Arrangement drawing.
Engineering Standards Book I
Engineering Standards Book II
Engineering Standards Book III
Engineering Standards Book IV
HPC Computer Aided Design and Drafting Standards Manual
4.5 Section 5, 6, and 7 of this procedure are intended to familiarize the reader with personnel
responsibilities, file management, and terminology prior to introducing the particulars ofthe
General Arrange drawings. These sections are followed by an illustrated overview of the ACHE
units intended to help familiarize the reader with unit components prior to discussing HPC
designing and detailing procedures. Designing issues pertain to the where or how components are
arranged and the detailing issues pertain to how the components are shown on the drawing.

5.0 RESPONSIBILITIES
5.1 Drafting
5.1.1 On new jobs, begin the General Arrangement drawing by using the Protoarc.dwt
template when launching AutoCAD. Use the HPC block library to complete the
detailing. Use the Hudson Products pull-down menu to insert title block, grid, and GA
notes. When feasible use a recent AutoCAD drawing that is overall similar in scope to
the job at hand.
5.1.2 Detailer responsibilities entail:
a. Completing General Arrangement drawing(s) per HPC standards.
b. Inquiring about input data discrepancies and design queries, and making informed
decisions and detailing accordingly. Inquires need to be directed to the assigned
Section Leader. When this is not possible direct inquires to another Section Leader,
Section Leader's assistant, or Drafting Supervisor.
c. Submitting check prints to Section Leader for checking. On revision submit the
VOID drawing as well.
d. Pulling the original hard copy of the drawing from the drawing cabinet and writing
VOID on it before beginning any revisions.
e. Back-checking and scrubbing drawings according to HPC procedure in Standard
Book I.
f. Maintaining drawing file per section 6.0 of this procedure.
5.1.3 Checker responsibilities entail:
Checking drawings per HPC standards outlined in the Checking and Back-Checking
Procedure and current job-related information.
5.1.4 Section Leader responsibilities entail:
a. Assigning General Arrangement detailing and checking work.
b. Ensuring Detailer has all available information significant for completing the GA.
c. Supervising Detailer and Checker to ensure accurate GA detailing and checking.
d. Resolving discrepancies between detailer and checker
e. Reviewing, approving, and signing-off on GA drawing(s)
f. Releasing GA drawings for engineering signature.
g. Issuing GA drawings to Document Control for distribution.
h. Providing the Issue Sequence/Release form to the detailer for confirmation offile
maintenance.
5.2 Structural Engineering is responsible for the following items.
5.2.1 Reviewing and signing-off on GA drawing(s).
5.2.2 Discussing and resolving drawing discrepancies with the Section Leader.
5.2.3 Returning signed GA drawing(s) to Section Leader.
GENERAL ARRANGEMENT DESIGN AND DETAILING REV. 1,4-05-02

6.0 FILE MAINTENANCE
6.1 File name format for GA drawing is #OOO_llX_RO;
where: #000 the alphanumeric job number with # representing the alphabet
11 series drawing number
X the alphabet identifying the unit bank
RO the latest revision
An underscore separates each factor; GA file name examples: HI23_llA_Rl, J045_llB_R2.
6.2 GA check-print files must be placed in the GA_CHECKING folder when the drawing is submitted
for checking. GA_CHECKING folder location:
VoI2(Q:)\HPC_CAD_SERVER\HPC_CAD_JOBS\TRANSFER FILES\GA_CHECKING
6.3 GA files must be retrieved from the GA_CHECKING folder for scrubbing.
6.4 GA drawing file is placed in the Checked_ISSUED job folder after the scrubbing phase is
completed. The Section Leader provides detailer the Issue Sequence/Release form and detailer
confirms file maintenance. Checked ISSUED folder location:
VoI2(Q:)\HPC_CAD_SERVER\HPC_CAD_JOBS\Checked_Issued\XOOO
6.5 In cases where the drawing in Checked_ISSUED is revised prior to issuance, the GA drawing file
is placed in the TO BE MOVED folder after being revised. TO BE MOVED folder location:
VoI2(Q:)\HPC_CAD_SERVER\HPC_CAD_JOBS\TRANSFER FILES\Sam\TO BE MOVED
6.6 Only after the approved drawing has been moved into the Checked_ISSUED or TO BE MOVED
folder should other file copies in the TRANSFER folder or hard drive be deleted.

8.0 UNIT COMPONENTS AND CONFIGURATION OVERVIEW
This section is an overview of basic induced and forced draft unit configurations. A unit configuration
consists of component requirements noted on the Fin-Fan® Spec. Sheet.
UNIT • Basic unit components-tube bundle(s), plenum or hood(s), fan, fan
ring(s), mechanical equipment, structural, and walkways. The figures
below illustrate the level layout of the basic unit components, minus
the structural and walkways.
• Basic optional unit components include louver and steam coil.
• Multi-bundle units consist of more than one tube bundle.
• Each will have a unit serial number located on the fan ring. (Example
#OOO-llA-A,where -A may = any alphabet; no omissions)
• Unit width is the width of the TBF. Multi-bundle unit width equals
total of bundle widths.
• Unit nominal length equals the tube length.

HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION
STD BOOK II, vol. I SECT. IA - PG. 8
TUBE BUNDLE I. Assembly of the heat exchanger pressure parts. One or more per unit.
• Consists of headers and tubes encased in a tube bundle frame.
• May perform the same service or each performs different services, or
any combination.
• Bundles performing the same service will have the same item number.
Header • Consist of header boxes, process nozzles, vent, drain, and instrument
connections.
• Header types include plug, cover-plate, and pipe.
• Each will have an item number located on the header nameplate.
Tube Bundle • Assembly of components encasing and supporting the tube bundle.
Frame (TBF)
• Components include side channels, tube supports, tube keepers,
header supports, spacers, and lifting lugs.
• Frame flanges may toe in or out.

PLENUM I • A hood is an Induced Draft unit component consisting of several
HOOD panels bolted together, located above the TBF.
• The plenum is a Force Draft unit component consisting of several
panels bolted together, located below the TBF.
• HPC standard height is 3 ft. for both plenums and hoods. The height is
increased in 1" increments when the minimum fan size requirement is
violated.

FAN I. Quantity of 1, 2, or 3 same size fans per unit; encased in a fan ring.
• Number of fans is determined by tube length, TBF width, and fan size
required for the process.
• AP (Adjustable Pitch) or AV (Auto-Variable®)
• Optional-AV air-line support, mounted atop fan ring or bottom panel
Fan Ring • Consist of a two- or four-piece assembly of components encasing the
fan.
• Components include ring channels and fan ring struts.
• Induced Draft-located above the TBF and mounted to the top hood
panels.
• Forced Draft-located below the TBF and mounted to the bottom
plenum panels.

STRUCTURAL I. Components include stub columns (forced draft units), main
columns, X- and Knee braces, and walkway support.
Stub Column • Forced Draft-basis of the plenum.
• Minimum of four per unit, with tube lengths equal-to or smaller­
than 32', maximum of eight for 3-fan units.
Main Column I. Forced Draft-supports the plenum. Center column required
when tube length greater-than 32'.
• Induced Draft-supports the TBF or SCBF.
X-Brace • Two angles connected in the middle and attached to main
column gussets at header end of unit.
• For units sharing columns, bracing is applied to the end units and
every other unit in between. On even number units two adjoining
units will have X-bracing.
Knee Brace • Two-angle assembly attached to main column gussets; minimum
of 2 at each column line.
• Must not interfere with machinery mount assembly.
Walkway • One beam and angles support assembly attached to column.
Support
• Supports the header walkway.

WINTERIZATION I. The basic unit component of a winterized unit is the same as
described for a non-winterized configuration.
• Remainder of the unit is walled in with steel wall and roof
panels.
• Grade-mounted units require no floor but do require curb angles
supporting the steel wall panels and! or louvers.
• Piperack-mounted units require mounting beams, floor beams,
and a complete steel floor.

9.0 GENERAL ARRANGEMENT REFERENCE AND STANDARD DRAWINGS
9.1 The standard drawings (11 SO I, II SD2, and so on) contain HPC standards and reference material
pertaining to designing, detailing, and dimensioning elements of the General Arrangement. The
information on the standard drawings is correlated with the information provided in section 10.0 of
this procedure.
9.2 The units illustrated on the standard drawings are compilations ofconditions pertaining to HPC
standard designs. The standard drawings illustrate and provide designing/detailing standards for
creating the GA. Rules for calculating dimensions as well as call-out requirements are also
provided on these drawings. These standarddrawings are to be used as examples ofwhatthe GA
drawing should resemble.
9.3 The appendices contain additional reference material from which information is acquired for the
GA grid and notes. The illustrations contain bold arrows and numbers that correspond to the
appendix notations outlining information that should be considered and/or used.
9.4 The first and foremost factor when using assorted documents is to ensure the job and item numbers
correlate. Compare applicable information between the reference material. Query discrepancies
between information, by checking the job package and the kick-off meeting notes then present the
issue to Section Leader. Resolve discrepancies prior to beginning the General Arrangement
drawing.
10.0 GENERAL ARRANGEMENT DRAWING
10.1 Terms shown in this section in ALL CAPS, TIMES NEW ROMAN BOLD font are examples of
GA terminology and should appear as shown in this section on the General Arrangement drawing.
10.2 The GA detailing package will contain KEY PLAN (optional), ANCHOR BOLT PLAN
(optional), PLAN or PLAN OF PLENUM, FRONT ELEVATION, SIDE ELEVATION, and
SUGGESTED LIFTING ARRANGEMENT drawings. These drawings may be considered
collectively as a GA package and each bank will require a GA package. Multi-item units will have
the item number under the dimension line at the bottom of or at the top of the bundle.
10.3 KEY PLANS are provided when multiple drawings are required to detail the plan and front
elevations of one bank.
10.3.1 The key plan is considered the first GA drawing for the bank and is listed as drawing
liA.
10.3.2 Shown is the top view of the unit, fans, walkways, and ladders; the illustration is very
similar to the plan or the plan of plenum illustration.
10.3.3 Column distances along the top and left side of unit illustration are dimensioned and
column identifications shown.
10.4 ANCHOR BOLT PLANS are provided for all winterized units without floors and per customer's
request.
10.4.1 All column centerlines and anchor bolts requirements are located on the Anchor Bolt
Plan.
10.4.2 Details of the column base plate, ladder base are shown on the Anchor Bolt Plan, space
permitting. These details are shown on the plan/plan of plenum when no anchor bolt plan
is required. Column base plate is based on grade or pipe rack mounting; see the Fin­
Fan® Spec. Sheet for type.

10.4.3 The Anchor Bolt plan is the second General Arrangement drawing if KEY PLAN is
required and listed as drawing 11 A 1. If no Key Plan is required then the Anchor Bolt
Plan follows the Plan drawing(s).
10.5 PLAN and PLAN OF PLENUM drawing (from here on referred to as plan; see abbreviations)
contains outline illustration of unit components from a top viewpoint. The plan is considered the
first General Arrangement drawing if the key plan and anchor bolt plan are not required.
10.5.1 This drawing shows the top view of the plenum on a Forced Draft unit and the top view
of the Induced Draft unit. This drawing contains the information grid, north arrow, and
GA notes.
10.5.2 The grid is an informational table containing information for each item in a bank.
a. The grid is located at the top left comer of the first plan or plan of plenum drawing.
b. The information for completing the grid is found on the FFSS and Header Design
WEIGHTS & WELD METAL sheets, and the structural engineering Weight.
c. The locations of input from the FFSS are shown on the standard drawings as (288­
22A), where 2 = Fin-Fan® spec-sheet page (lSI, 2nd , or 3rd ), 88 = spec­
sheet,22 = spec-sheet line number,andA = spec-sheet
column (A, B, or C).
d. Place a "-" in blank grid boxes to demonstrate that information is not applicable.
10.5.3 A north arrow is placed on the plan drawing and located as close to the plan detail as
possible. When the north direction is not known add the word ASSUMED under the
north arrow illustration.
10.5.4 Columns identifications are located from left to right beginning with the number 1 and
sequentially increasing for each column, and alphabetized from top to bottom beginning
with A and sequentially ascending for each column.
10.5.5 GA notes are located on the right side of the first plan drawing. All note requirements
shown below appear on the GA, in the sequence and wording shown below. Use the GA
NOTES block located in the HPC pull-down menu. When a note is not applicable to the
job list NOT APPLICABLE for the note. On RO drawings place additional notes to the
bottom of the notes ensuring the WORK THIS DRAWING WITH: note is the last note.
On revisions, place additional notes after the WORK THIS DRAWING WITH: note.
1. VENTIDRAIN: this note contains vent and drain information listed in an a, b, c
format. List the information as folIowing a. VENT: followed by b. DRAIN: . Each
listing will have the size and flange type followed by its location on header. The
location is noted as (WITH BLIND FLANGE (optional» LOCATED ON
CENTERLINE OF HEADER AT TOP or BOTTOM OF INLET and/or
OUTLET, and/or RETURN HEADER. If more than one item is shown on FRONT
ELEVATION drawing, add the following notes for each connection: FOR ITEM
(S): 00000. (SEE FRONT ELEVATION FOR LOCATION). Additional
connections are alphabetically listed. (If vent or drain is not required, add NOT
APPLICABLE for the a. or b. listing). E.g., a. VENT: 1 1/2"-150# LWNRF wi
BLIND FLANGE LOCATED ON CL OF HEADER AT TOP OF INLET HEADER;
b. DRAIN: 1 1/2"-150# LWNRF wi BLIND FLANGE LOCATED ON CL OF
HEADER AT BOTTOM OF RETURN HEADER.

2. INSTRUMENT CONNECTIONS: this note will contain pressure, temperature
and/or cleaning connection information listed in an a, b, c, format. List the
information as: a. PRESSURE CONNECTION: followed by b. TEMPERATURE
CONNECTION: then c. CLEANING CONNECTION:, add the size-#'s and type,
followed by the location of connection on header or nozzle. Follow the note formats
listed above, as well as the item identification in (l), and list each item separately.
E.g., a. PRESSURE CONNECTION:
3. NOZZLE COVER REQUIREMENTS: HPC standard note is TO HAVE ... FOR
SHIPPING. Ifthe job calls for special requirements such as with gasket or a
particular type of cover then add the information in the appropriate place; e.g.,
"...PLASTIC COVER..." or "...WITH NEOPRENE GASKET."
4. NITROGEN PURGE REQUIREMENTS: YES or NOT APPLICABLE option.
5. PIPING NOTE: HPC standard note is ALL TUBE BUNDLE FRAMES ARE
DESIGNED FOR 5/16" MOVEMENT IN EITHER HORIZONTAL
DIRECTION PERPENDICULAR TO TUBES. Movement may vary; if required
add"...FRAME FOR ITEM 00000 IS DESIGNED..." .
6. BEARING: or COUPLING: HPC standard bearings are HPC No. 50081 (TOP)
and HPC No. 50082 (BOTTOM), for 5' to 9' fan diameters, or HPC No. 50080
(BOTTOM) for fan diameters 10' and greater. On gear jobs list the coupling
manufacturer and model. (e.g., REXNORD 200 or REXNORD SERI ES 71-225)
I I
7. DRIVE: on belt-driven units list the manufacturer and name brand (e.g., GATES
POLY CHAIN® or GATES PowerGrip®) and on gear-driven units list the
manufacturer and model, (e.g., AMARILLO)
8. VIBRATION SWITCH: list manufacturer, type, and model (e.g.,
MURPHY S PST VS- 2-EX orMETRIX 5175 -123). Other notation such as
I I I
sensor, mounting hardware, or wiring diagram information may be listed as per
required by customer or section leader. (reminder: if no vibration switch is required
list NOT APPLICABLE for this note)
9. VALVE POSITIONER: list manufacturer. This is required only on certain AV fans
(e.g., MOORE)
10. LOUVER MATERIAL: separately list frame and blade material as ALUMINUM
or GALVANIZED STEEL.
(e.g., FRAME: 10 GA. GALVANIZED STEEL or FRAME : ALUMINUM
BLADE: 16 GA. GALVANIZED STEEL BLADE : ALUMINUM )
11. LOUVER OPERATION: this note will contain the operation type, actuator
manufacturer and model, control feature, and blade action. List the operation as
either MANUAL or AUTO. For automatic-operated louvers list the actuator (e.g.,
FISHER No. 656 -40); if dual and/or applicable, list the manual operator (e.g.,
SIDE MOUNTED KEYSTONE HANDWHEEL) and the louver controls as OPEN ON
AIR FAILURE or CLOSE ON AIR FAILURE. Add the blade action note
LOUVER BLADES TO BE PARALLEL ACTION or OPPOSED ACTION.
12. FOUNDATION AND ANCHOR BOLTS: HPC standard note is TO BE
FURNISHED BY OTHER

13. COLOR CODES: acquire the color code from the following lists, e.g., BLUE,

14. COATING: HPC standard note is SEE DWG Cl.
15. WALKWAY & LADDERS: HPC standard note is PER HPC STANDARDS
THAT COMPLY WITH OSHA.
16. PREASSEMBLY REQUIREMENTS: typical note is BASE UNIT or ALL
UNITS TO BE PREASSEMBLED or ONE or ALL UNIT(S) TO RUN-IN.
Additional testing will be located within this note; check the Fin-Fan® Specification
Sheet REMARK section and the customer specifications in the job package for
additional requirements. If no run-in is required do not list the note on the GA. (if
this requirement does not apply list NOT APPLICABLE)
17. SHOP ASSEMBLY: HPC standard note is COMPLETE, LESS LOWER
SUBSTRUCTURE, WALKWAYS, & LADDERS. Add or delete components as
required.
18. SHIP UNIT: this note states the shipping requirements. Most commonly this note
will reference the shop assembly note, e.g., PER NOTE 17, LESS MOTORS,
MOTOR MOUNTS, BELTS, AND BELT GUARDS.
19. COLUMN LOADS: HPC standard note is SEE REACTION CHART RC#. The
reaction chart drawing numbering system is 11A = RC1,11B = RC2,11C =
RC3, and so on.
20. BUNDLE COVER REQUIREMENTS: TO HAVE COVERS FOR SHIPPING.
Ifa specific type ofcover is required then list it accordingly; " ...HAVE 3/8"
PLYWOOD COVERS•.."
21. FIREPROOFING REQUIREMENTS: list fireproofing inforrnation as state in the
job package. If necessary, verify notation with Section Leader.
22. BUG SCREEN REQUIREMENTS: list the material, size, and type.
23. WIND SKIRT REQUIREMENTS: list the material, size, and type.
24. REMOVABLE FAN ASSEMBLY REQUIREMENTS: list YES or NO.
25. RTD REQUIREMENTS: add part number and note if SHOP or FIELD
ASSEMBLED.
26. METRIC REQUIREMENTS: HPC standard note is ALL DIMENSIONS ARE
MILLIMETERS; NUMBERS IN [ ] ARE FEET AND/OR INCHES.

27. WORK THIS DRAWING WITH: this note is required when more than one

10.5.6 Fan designations are shown for every fan on the plan drawing.
a. The designation is placed near the motor symbol..
b. The designation format is xxoa- 0, where xx AP or AV (Adjustable Pitch or
'=
Auto-Variable®), 00 fan diameter, and -0 number of blades.
'= '=
(e.g., APll-6 and the designation is underlined)
c. Optional features are noted below the designation as wi 2-SPEED when 2-speed
motor is required on a AP fan, wi VP when Valve Positioner is required on an AV
fan, and wi BR when a Bias Relay is required on an AV fan.
10.5.7 TYPICAL FAN ROTATION notation and clockwise rotation arrow are shown on the
plan and placed on the first top left fan of each item.
10.5.8 Fan diameters should be reviewed to ensure the fan size is within the maximum
requirement outlined on the Table 3 on drawing IISD3.
10.6 FRONT ELEVATION
10.6.1 This drawing shows a front view of the unit(s)
10.6.2 Outlines of all visible unit components from this viewpoint are shown; i.e., nozzles,
TBF, plenum, fan ring, mechanical components, substructure, steam coil, louvers and
actuator, ladders, AV support, hail guard, and so on.
10.6.3 Use nozzle dimensions shown on proposal drawing for GA drawing. Otherwise, nozzle
dimensions should be shown in even dimension, e.g., 6'-2 \12, round to 6'-2.
10.6.4 The column spacing varies and is governed by the bundle width and the fan size. The
minimum column spacing for forced draft units should be 6" greater than the fan
diameter.
10.7 SIDE ELEVATION
10.7.1 This drawing shows as many side views as necessary to completely illustrate the unit.
10.7.2 For a multi-bundle unit show a side view of the complete unit and the bundle nearest the
view angle and also show a side section of only the tube bundle(s) from the same
viewing point. If applicable, include steam coil and louvers for that tube bundle. Under
the heading add the note (pARTS NOT SHOWN SAME AS ITEM 00000).
10.7.3 For winterized units with exterior wall view is shown on the side elevation and should
illustrate the outside wall panels, door, roof panels, and structural the unit components.
10.8 SUGGESTED LIFTING ARRANGEMENT
10.8.1 This arrangement is provided for jobs requiring any assembly of unit.
10.8.2 The drawing is very similar to the front and side elevation drawings minus the lower
substructure, bracing, walkways, and ladders. Show overall width, height and length
dimensions.
10.8.3 Shipping beams and cradles are shown in hidden line format.
10.8.4 Lifting beam with components is shown in hidden line format; call-out who will be
furnishing this component.

10.9 TUBE BUNDLE
10.9.1 Outlines of the tube bundle frame, headers, and nozzles are shown on the plan for
induced draft units. These parts do not need to be dimensioned.
10.9.2 TBF and all process nozzles, vent and drain are shown and dimensioned horizontally and
vertically on the front and side elevations. These components are shown but not
dimensioned on the suggested lifting arrangement.
10.9.3 Process nozzles and LWN instrument connections on the rear header on the front
elevation view are shown in hidden line format. Dimension the process nozzles, but only
identify the LWN instrument connections.
10.9.4 Process nozzles nearest the view angle of the side elevation are shown and dimensioned.
10.9.5 Slope direction and requirements is shown on the side elevation.
10.10 MECHANICAL
10.10.1 Motors with conduit boxes ~re outlined and shown for every fan illustration on the plan.
Dimension, once per each item, the location of the motor center to the centerline of fan
on the plan.
10.10.2 Gear drives are shown with motor and gear on the plan and dimensioned to the centerline
of the unit fan.
10.10.3 Gear drives are shown with the motor in a horizontal shaft position, suspended from the
fan ring on the front and side elevations, and the suggested lifting arrangement.
10.10.4 Outlines of the motor, machinery mount side channel, motor mount, conduit box, and
belt guard are shown on the front elevation. Dimension vertically the machinery mount
depth to the bottom of the fan ring.
10.10.5 Outlines of the machinery mount side channels, motor, motor mount, conduit box,
hangers, and vibration switch are shown on the side elevation. Dimension vertically the
location of the vibration switch to the bottom of the machinery mount.
10.10.6 Removable Fans do not differ in fan detailing practices, except for the addition ofthe
REMOVABLE FANS notation under the section heading ofthe plan.
10.11 PLENUM, HOOD, FAN RING, and INLET BELL
10.11.1 Outlines of the plenum, hood, fan rings, and inlet bell are shown on the front elevation
along with a 3" x 6" rectangle indicating the unit serial number plate and its location.
10.11.2 The plenum and fan-ring are dimensioned vertically from the bottom of the TBF or
SCBF to the bottom of the fan ring on the front elevation.
10.11.3 The hood and fan-ring are dimensioned vertically from the top of the TBF or louver on
the front elevation.
10.11.4 The plenum and hood height is increased in 1" increments when the minimum fan size
requirement is violated.
10.11.5 Note the INLET BELL on the front elevation.
10.12 FAN GUARD
10.12.1 Fan guards are required on forced draft unit, provided per customer's request on induced
draft units but recommended for induced draft units with hood walkways.
GENERAL ARRANGEMENT DESIGN AND DETAILING REV. 1,4-05-02

10.12.2 On induced draft units, fan guards are shown on the front and side. Guards are not shown
on the plan for clarity.
10.12.3 Note the fan guards with FAN GUARD note.
10.13 SUBSTRUCTURE
10.13.1 Column outlines are shown without cap plates on the plan.
10.13.2 Stub columns, induced draft main columns, and extended columns are shown on the
plan.
10.13.3 Shared main columns are not shown on the plan because the T-beam obstructs the view.
10.13.4 Header walkway support beams are shown on the plan.
10.13.5 Column designations on the front and side elevations correlate with the column
identifications on the plan.
10.13.6 Column spacing is dimensioned horizontally on center. Dimension vertically to locate
column splice and overall column height.
10.13.7 Angle and column bracing are shown with a single line and the angle or column partially
illustrated.
10.14 WALKWAYSandLADDERS
10.14.1 Header walkway, hood walkway, and ladder outlines are shown on the plan drawing;
mechanical walkways and ladders under the unit are shown in hidden line format. The
mechanical walkway width and lengths are dimensioned on the plan.
10.14.2 A walkway surface symbol (grating or checkered plate) is shown for each walkway on
the plan, except walkways under the unit.
10.14.3 Header walkway and ladders are not shown on the front elevation for clarity.
10.14.4 Top of grating or checkered plate is indicated with a note on the side elevations and on
the front elevation if walkway is shown.
10.14.5 Side-access walkways and ladders are shown partially on the front elevation and
dimensioned vertically to locate them relative to nearest column.
10.14.6 Header walkway, mechanical walkway, hood walkways, and extended ladders are shown
on the side elevation.
10.14.7 Mechanical walkways are dimensioned horizontally and vertically from bottom of
column to locate it relative to the center line of unit.
10.14.8 Hood walkways are dimensioned vertically from the top ofthe TBF to the top of floor
material. Header walkways are dimensioned vertically from the bottom of the TBF or
SCBF to the top of floor material.
10.14.9 All ladder centerline will be located with a CL LADDER notation.
10.14.10 Show support beams on the front and side elevations. Show floor beams on the side
elevation. Note beam size and description if known.
10.14.11 If side access walkway extends off support beam, show floor plate symbol and
dimension vertically to locate floor beams and customer supports to column. Note beam
and floor plate sizes and descriptions if known.
GENERAL ARRANGEMENT DESIGN AND DETAILING REV. 1, 4-05-02

By: Barnes, Carbrey
Date: 01-09-2025, Rev: 0

I I I I
HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION
STD BOOK II, vol. I SECT. lA - PG. 25
10.14.12 Ladders for hood walkway are located horizontally and vertically from the bottom of
column.
10.15 WINTERIZAnON COMPONENTS
10.15.1 Walls enclosing the unit are shown outlined on the plan.
10.15.2 Doors are usually located at opposite ends of a unit but may be located per Customer's
request and are shown partially opened on the plan.
10.15.3 A walkway notation is shown on the side elevation.
10.15.4 End re-circulation areas are shown on the plan and side elevation.
a. The depth of the end re-circulation area is called out on the Fin-Fan® spec. sheet.
b. The depth of the end re-circulation area may be increased (verify with section
leader) to clear header walkway door; allow minimum 9" clearance from outside
wall to edge of door.
c. Dimension horizontally off column for depth and width.
d. Dimension vertically from bottom of column to top of column or top deck.
10.15.5 Side re-circulation areas are shown on the plan and front elevations.
a. The width of this area is specified on the Fin-Fan Spec. Sheet.
b. The width of area may be increased, with section leader approval, to accommodate
HPC 2' x 2' access door; allow for 3" clearance between edge of column and
access door and round up to even figure.
c. Dimension horizontally from column centers.
10.15.6 Top re-circulation ducts are shown on the front and side elevations.
a. Show the end and roof panels and structural components, e.g., mounting beam.
b. Dimension vertically from the top of TBF to bottom of exhaust louver.
10.15.7 On side elevations show a minimum of two unit views; one showing the wall panels, roof
panels and doors, and the other showing the basic unit components. The view showing
the basic unit components is at column line of exterior wall. Note the column line view
under the heading as AT COL LINE 5, LOOKING WEST; direction may vary. Note
the viewing direction of exterior wall under the heading as LOOKING WEST; direction
may vary.
10.15.8 An access door is located on the by-pass louver end of the unit. HPC standard door is 2'
x 2' and will be noted on the front elevation as 2' x 2' DOOR (FS) (TVP) or (NS)
(TVP).
10.16 PIPERACKS
10.16.1 Piperack view is sectioned and shown on the plan in hidden line format.
10.16.2 Show support beams outlines in solid line format and the floor beam in hidden line
format.
10.16.3 Customer supports will be dimensioned off unit center and shown in hidden-line format
on the plan, front and side elevation.
10.17 FIREPROOFING
GENERAL ARRANGEMENT DESIGN AND DETAILING REV. 1,4-05-02

STD BOOK II, vol. I SECT. IA - PG. 26
10.17.1 Components to be fireproofed are outlined which represents the fireproofing thickness
are added to the columns and are shown on the front and side elevation.
10.17.2 Dimension vertically the extent of area to be fireproofed.
10.18 LOUVERS
10.18.1 Show louver outlines on the front and side elevation, and suggested lifting arrangement.
10.18.2 Dimension vertically for louver depth on the front and side elevations. HPC standard
louver depths is7 W' and 4 %" for Canadian jobs. Increase louver depth to 9 W' when
hail guards are required.
10.18.3 HPC standard louver depth is 12" when used on induced draft units.
10.18.4 The louver operators are shown on the front and side elevations at end opposite inlet end.
This placement prevents interference with piping.
10.18.5 By-pass louver and actuator outlines are shown on the front elevation and on the
appropriate side elevation. Indicate and describe the louver operator and actuator type.
By-pass louvers may be linked to exhaust louvers and operated with one actuator.
10.18.6 Exhaust louver with actuator located at the unit ends is shown partial in solid line form
on the front and side elevations. Indicate and describe the louver operator and actuator
type.
10.18.7 Side and end intake louvers and louver blades outlines are shown on the front and side
elevations. Dimension from bottom of unit column to top of intake louver.
10.19 STEAM COILS
10.19.1 Steam coil frame outlines are shown on the front and side elevations, and suggested
lifting arrangement.
10.19.2 Inlet and outlet nozzles are dimensioned horizontally and vertically on both the front and
side elevations. Note nozzles as near side (NS) or far side (FS) on the front elevation.
10.20 AV AIR-LINE SUPPORT
10.20.1 On forced draft units, show in solid-line format on the plan and in hidden-line format on
the side elevation and the suggested lifting arrangement. Dimension vertically from top
of bottom panel to center of support pipe. The support is located 6" offthe fan center and
dimensioned to the center of the fan.
10.20.2 On induced draft units shown in solid-line format on the plan, side elevation, and the
suggested lifting arrangement. Dimensions vertically from the top of fan ring to center of
support pipe on the side elevation.
10.21 HAIL GUARD
10.21.1 Hail guard placement varies to above TBF, inside louver, atop fan ring.
10.21.2 Hail guards on forced draft units are shown on the side elevation as a hidden line placed
above of the TBF.
10.21.3 Hail guards on forced draft units with louver are shown on the side elevation as a hidden
line inside the louver box placed below the top of the louver.
10.21.4 On Chittom louvers the hail guards are framed and set atop the louver box.
10.21.5 Hail guards on induced draft units are shown using the fan guard symbol.

10.21.6 Hail guards require no dimensioning but are noted as HAIL GUARD 1 x 1/8 GALV
GRGT when atop the TBF. On induced draft units add wi HAIL GUARD to the fan
guard note when applicable.
10.22 MAINTENANCE GRIDS
10.22.1 The maintenance grid is an optional component for induced draft units only.
10.22.2 The grid is shown with a 4' hidden line slightly above the top of the TBF on the front
and side elevations.
10.22.3 Dimensions are not required, but do note with MAINTENANCE GRID 4' x 4' (TYP)
on the side elevation view. Also list the grid material; HPC standard is 1" x 3/16"
GALV SMOOTH GRTG (TYP) on the side elevation view.
10.23 WIND SKIRTS
10.23.1 Windskirt outlines are shown on the front and side elevations.
10.23.2 The Fin-Fan® Specification Sheet may note the dimension for the windskirt.
10.24 MATCH LINES
10.24.1 Match line is required when an item consists of too many units to show on one drawing.
10.24.2 The match line is located at a column center between units.
10.24.3 Place MATCH LINE above and SEE DWG llA? at the bottom of the match line
notation; where? = drawing number containing matching unit (5).
10.25 TITLE BLOCK
10.25.1 Obtain title block information, customer's name, plant location, purchase order number,
and job number from the FFSS (lines 5-7).
10.25.2 Obtain drawing number, item number, and bank identification from the Drawing
Schedule. Verify item number, bank designation, and drawing number in the Visibility
system.
10.25.3 Add the detailer's initials and drawing date prior to submitting the drawing for checking.
10.25.4 Add checker's, Section Leader's, and Engineer's initials and associated dates after
completing the scrubbing phase.
11.0 REVISIONS
11.1 Detailers:
11.1.1 Complete all revisions using the GA file located in the Checked_ISSUED job folder.
Checked ISSUED folder location:
VoI2(Q:)\llPC_CAD_SERVER\llPC_CAD_JOBS\Checked_Issued\XOOO
11.1.2 OPEN the drawing and do SAVE_AS placing the drawing onto the hard drive and rename
the new drawing with the latest revision number, _Rl. Follow file-naming format in
section 6.0.
11.1.3 Pull the hard copy ofthe drawing(s) from the drawing file and write VOID on it/them.
11.1.4 Document all changes after issuance as revisions by placing the latest revision triangle
near the revision.

11.1.5 Use of one revision triangle, in the vicinity of revisions, is sufficient for large numbers of
revisions (refer to the Section Leader for guidance). Revision triangles are not required
when the entire drawing is revised, but clearly describe the revision.
11.1.6 Clearly describe revisions and avoid using such statements as REVISED PER CUST
TRANSMITTAL.
11.1.7 Check the job stick file, review or approval drawing, and original drawing for additional
revisions.
11.1.8 Initial, add comments and date the revision block after completing the revisions. Add
approval initials after checking and approval of revisions.
11.1.9 Maintain drawing files as outlined in Section 6.0 of this procedure.

11.3 Document Control maintains the original drawing(s).

7A The infonnation in the GENERAL DESIGN section pertains to the bundle width, slope, and multi-bundle infonnation.
7B/7C HEADER infonnation such as type, tube rows and passes, and split requirements should be compared with other infonnation if
possible; e.g., header design or bundle worksheet. List the TUBE length (15C) in the GA grid.
I7B Compare NOZZLE infonnation to any available resources, i.e., header design or bundle work sheets. The inlet and outlet nozzle
size, rating, and facing are listed on the GA grid.
20A Compare STRUCTURAL - WALKWAY infonnation with the WALKWAY & LADDER specification on page three of the spec
sheets. Mounting (2IA) is listed as Grade (unit sits at ground level) or Piperack (sometimes listed as Structure; unit sits on beams
located above ground level).
31A FAN infonnation is used to detail the GA and called-out on the plan drawing.
31B Use DRIVER infonnation to detennine the fan center distance; some infonnation is listed in the GA grid and notes. 2-speed motors
are shown on the GA as 00/00 where 00 = 378. Motors may be 100% or 50% 2-speed.
3IC List SPEED REDUCER infonnation in the GA notes
38C List VIBRATION SWITCH infonnation in plain view on the PLAN and include in the GA notes.
46 Use HEATING COIL infonnation to detail the steam coil bundle located under the TBF. The nozzle infonnation on line 57 is listed
in the GA grid.
46C AIR RECIRCULATION pertains to winterization and appears in YESINO fonnat. When YES, the TYPE blank should contain the
type and size requirements; EXTERNAL-SIDE refers to over-the-side design and EXTERNAL-END refers to over-the-end design.
49C LOUVER infonnation should be provided for winterized units (46C should have YES), otherwise the
louver is located atop the TBF.
55C MISCELLANEOUS infonnation pertains to guards and bug screens. Fan guards are always provided on forced draft units but only
at customer's request on induced draft units.
GENERAL ARRANGEMENT DESIGN AND DETAILING REV. 1,4-05-02

By: Barnes, Carbrey

HPC Fin-Fan® Specification Sheet, Page 3 of 3
7B (Process) nozzle cover requirements and connection locations are provided in this section. List this information in the GA notes.
29C The information below the ASSEMBLY & BAY TESTING is used to complete the GA notes (see section 10.5.5 of this
procedure).
38A Information below the WALKWAY & LADDERS is used for designing purposes. Compare this information with the walkway
information under section STRUCTURAL-WALKWAYS on page 2 of the spec. sheet; 20A. If there are discrepancies, check for
the latest spec sheet., the job package, and kick-off meeting notes, then present the problem to Section Leader.
38B The louver information under the CONTROL-AIR FAILURE section is used in the GA notes.
38C The LOUVER ACTUATOR information in this section contains model numbers that are called-out on the GA front and side
elevations. If the by-pass louver is linked to another louver it will be noted in this section and should be shown as such on the
elevations.
43B/C ACCESSORIES are specified in a YESINO format. The Spreader Bar requirements may be noted as DESIGN & DETAIL, if
required. On the lifting arrangements, note the spreader bar as BY OTHERS or HPC. If a removable fan assembly is required,
check that an 'R' follows the Model designation on page 1 of spec sheets. Question any discrepancies with Section Leader. The
VFD control information is shown under the motor grid blank.
53 The REMARKS section may at times contain additional information on various components. Do not overlook the REMARK
section or assume the line requirements are the sole source of information.

The proposal drawing should be viewed as a guide to the unit configuration. Compare unit type, size, and configuration information, as
well as the optional component requirements, to your Fin-Fan® Specification Sheet. Generally the Fin-Fan® Specification Sheet is correct;
however, you should not assume this if several discrepancies occur.
Comparable information:
I. Unit type and configuration, e.g., forced or induced draft, piperack or grade mounting, and so on.
2. Unit size
3. Nozzle requirements
4. Optional components, e.g., walkways, louvers, stearn coils, and so on.

Compare the row and number of tubes, the plate lengths, and so forth with the header design infonnation.
The Fin-Fan® Specification Sheet and Header Design Sketch indicate if offset nozzles are required. To detennine an offset nozzle
requirement see page 2 of spec sheet, line 13B; if the number of passes is greater than the number of tube rows, the header design sketch
will contain a front section showing the offset direction. Once it is detennined that offset nozzles are required, acquire the TUBE LAYOUT
document and calculate the nozzle placement(s) as instructed below.
Steps for detennining offset nozzle location from center of header:
I. Detennine header width, including end plates, and locate center of header.
2. Detennine distance c/c of outmost tubes of the first pass.
3. Locate offset inlet nozzle at center of first pass and dimension to center of column; round off as required.
4. Repeat steps to locate off-set outlet nozzle in relation to the last pass.

STD BOOK HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION SECT. 2A -PG. 1
MECHANICAL WORKSHEET
1.0 PURPOSE & INTRODUCTION
1.1 The MWS exists to layout the drive arrangement for ACHE units. It is primarily used as a
reference worksheet for arrangement and detail drawings as well as bills of materials.
When required, it is issued to the customer.
1.2 Throughout this work instruction, references are made to drawings (written as A-#, EX#, or
REF#) that can be found in the appendix ofthis document.
1.2.1 The electronic files for all 'A-#' drawings are not located in the normal server
directory. They can be found on the Macintosh server at:
HPC-SAVOY Ethernet\CAD SERVER\*STANDARDS\MECHANICAL WORKSHEET
1.2.2 There are no electronic files ofthe drawings number with EX# or REF#. The
original hard copies are stored in the Standards department.
1.3 There are also masters stored on the Macintosh server in the location shown in paragraph
1.2.1, above.
2.0 CONTENTS
1.0 PURPOSE & INTRODUCTION 1
2.0 CONTENTS 1
3.0 ASSOCIATED DOCUMENTS 2
4.0 OWNERSHIP AND ISSUANCE 2
5.0 FORCED AND INDUCED DRAFT BELT DRIVES .2
6.0 FORCED DRAFT GEAR DRIVES 6
7.0 INDUCED DRAFT GEAR DRIVES 8
8.0 REVISIONS 10
APPENDIX 11
MECHANICAL WORKSHEET REV.-U; FI8=99
Data Issued
By: Barnes, Carbrey
Date: 01-09-2025, Rev: 0

STD BOOK HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION SECT. 2A -PC. 2
3.0 ASSOCIATED DOCUMENTS
3.1 The following items may be affected by MWS changes.
Drawmg Schedule
Fan Order Fonn
TBFWS (Induced Draft)
Coating Sheet
General Arrangement Dwg. (11 Series)
Unit Assembly Dwg. (10 Series)
Machinery Mount Dwg. (4 Series)
Shaft Dwg.
Parts List
Recommended Spare Parts List
Visibility® BOMs
FFSS
3.2 If the MWS is changed, these should also be checked for changes. Conversely, a change in
any of these may affect the MWS.
4.0 OWNERSHIP AND ISSUANCE
4.1 The MWS is created by Drafting as a reproducible of one of the master sheets or of an
existing MWS.
4.2 The MWS is checked and scrubbed by Drafting.
4.3 After completion, the MWS is given to the Section Leader for issuance.
4.4 The original tracing must be signed by a Fan Engineer. The Section Leader runs a copy for
Structural Engineering and, when required, delivers to Document Control, who issues to
the customer per sheet no's.
4.5 After issuance to customer, Document Control runs a copy to give to the Section Leader for
the drafting file and files the original in the flat file for future reference. If not issued to
customer, the Section Leader files the MWS in the drafting file.
5.0 FORCED AND INDUCED DRAFT BELT DRIVES
5.1 The MWS for belt drive units is to be filled out per example documents MWS-EXI and
MWS-EX2.
5.2 Select Drive:
5.2.1 Get the following infonnation from the FFSS, if available.
Job no.
customer name & location (use GA if available)
customer's purchase order number (from job package)
item number(s)
number of fans
motor manufacturer, type, HP, RPM, V, PH, Hz
fan dia., blade type, no. of blades, AP/AV, speed ratio, tip speed
5.2.2 Get type of drive from the FFSS.
5.2.2.1 HPC standard for belt drives is Gates.
5.2.2.2 Dayco is the HPC standard for V-belt type drives (use Dayco catalog).

StD BOOK HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION SECt. zA -PC. 3
5.2.2.3 Standard service factor is 1.8 for HSD synchronous belt drives and 1.4
for V-belt type drives. The service factor may vary per the job
package or customer specifications.
5.2.3 Woods drives (HSD or V-belt)
5.2.3.1 Use the HPC standard drive selection chart to find a drive arrangement
with a reference center distance (C.D.). If drive is not in the selection
chart, use a similar drive as a reference (round the C.D. to the nearest
1/4" increment on the worksheet).
5.2.3.2 Use the Woods program to find drive data per these instructions:
og on to the drive computer through tne
Woods program.
Select (1) for Standard OEM COST and (1) for V-belt or (3) for HSD drives. Select (2) for input
SERVICE FACTOR and type in the appropriate factor.
Enter the following data at the appropriate prompts:
Driver Horsepower is the motor HP from the FFSS.
Driver RPM is the motor RPM from the FFSS.
Driver shaft diameter is based on the motor frame size.
(refer to drawing A-I if Siemens or Marathon, otherwise refer to the manufacturer's
Motor Data Sheet)
Driven RPM is the fan RPM from the FFSS.
Driven shaft diameter is 2.75 standard.
Min. Center Distance is the reference C.D. from the Drive Selection Chart.
At the new screen, enter (2)-(6) to change inputs, (8) to exit, or (1) to continue.
After continuing, select (1) to consider ALL Drives. For V-belt, select (1) for ALL Belts and (1)
for ALL Sheaves.
If drives are available which meet criteria, they will be shown. Ifno drives meet the design then
modify the inputs; use the catalog to find an available drive, or switch to a different type ofdrive.
Use "P" to print the options page, then select line number ofdrive which has an output RPM and
C.D. closest to the design value.
At the drive information screen, Use "L" to add a label to the page (i.e., "JOB GOOD, ITEM E ­
123"). Use "P" to print the design.
Select "E" to exit the program when finished.
5.2.3.3 In lieu ofthis program, the Woods catalog may be used to find drive
data.
5.2.3.4 Use "FH" sprockets in lieu of standard "H" sprockets where applicable.
These "FH" sprockets use smaller type E bushings in lieu ofthe
bushings normally supplied (refer to drawing A-5).
5.2.4 Gates drives (HSD or V-belt; and all Polychain drives)
5.2.4.1 Use the HPC standard Drive Selection Chart to size the drive, or find
the reference center distance and use the Gates program or catalog
(round the C.D. to the nearest 1/4" increment on the worksheet).
5.2.4.2 Use the Gates Program to find the drive data per these instructions:
MECHANICAL WORKSHEET REV. 0, 1-18=99

og on to drive computer through the MS-DOS prompt "e:\>". Type "GATES", then select In
order "Connect Via List OfHosts...", "Main #", "Call". Wait for logon ID = HPC. Password =
LONE. If shown, accept defaults for computer or monitor.
At RAD System Menu, select "Design Flexibility" using keyboard scroll arrows then [enter]. Keep
hitting [enter] until the MAIN MENU is shown. Select" 1" for Run Design Flex Program, then
select "1" for HSD or "2" for V-belt. Select "3" for Design New Drive.
Enter the following data at the appropriate prompts:
For NEMA motors, set NEMA standards to [Y] to scroll through available HP and RPM
values (using space bar), use [enter] to select
For non-NEMA motors, set NEMA standards to [N] and enter HP and RPM
DriveR shaft diameter is based on the motor frame size
(refer to drawing A-I if Siemens or Marathon, otherwise refer to the manufacturer's
Motor Data Sheet)
Use default Pulley aD of 0.00
Enter ratio as "Speed Down Ratio" or toggle to "DriveN RPM" and enter fan RPM (leave "to"
= 0.00).
DriveN shaft aD is 2.75 standard.
Use default Pulley aD of 0.00.
Enter the service factor.
Enter the reference C.D. from the Drive Selection Chart (± 10%) (leave "to" = 0.00), or type
in a range which is ±2" from the reference C.D.
Trapezoidal belt is toggled to "NO" (using the space bar).
Toggle either Powergrip HTD or Polychain to "YES"
Maximum Drive Top Width is O.
After all inputs, press the [ESC] key to continue.
Select"1" to sort by relative cost and show all available drives.
Use [Print Screen] key to print options screen then use scroll arrows and <ENTER> to select the
drive which has an output RPM and C.D. closest to the design value, or [ESC] to go back and
change the input data.
To print the selected drive, select 0 to see notes, then "2" to Print Selected Drive. For customer
application, add label (i.e., "JOB GOOD, ITEM E-123").
Select defaults for printing options then [ESC], toggle [YES] for noise information then [ESC] to
print.
After printing, to quit program type "99", "9", [ESC] (YES), [ESC] (YES), and "CD\" [enter] to
return to "C:\>" drive.
5.2.4.3 In lieu of using this program, the catalog may be used to find drive
data.
5.2.4.4 Use "F" sprockets in lieu ofstandard "P" sprockets where applicable.
These "F" sprockets use smaller type E bushings in lieu ofthe
bushings normally supplied (refer to drawing A-5).
5.3 Select form:
5.3.1 Select motor frame size from drawing A-6.
5.3.1.1 For non-NEMA motors, get the motor frame dimensions from an
appropriate catalog and select a motor mount appropriate for the motor
frame.
5.3.1.2 Use drive picture from catalog, fan diameter, motor frame size, and
MM depth to select the correct worksheet master (refer to drawing A­
7) in this section and in the Worksheet Masters Book.

STD BOOK HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION SECT. 2A -PC. 5
5.3.2 Run a reproducible of the selected master.
5.4 Fill in data along the right side of form from the FFSS, job package, and drawings in the
appendix. Pay special attention to the following:
5.4.1 MM width = 2'-6 for 5' through 7' fans, 3'-6 for fans 8' and up.
5.4.2 Using bushing sizes, get keyway information from drawing A-2. Ifnon-square
key with shaft, check "wi bush". If square key with shaft, check "wi shaft".
5.4.3 The inlet bell set number comes from drawing A-3.
5.4.4 For fan information, ifno valve positioner is required, erase "1701 W" under
"V.P.". If bias relay is required, erase "V.P.: 1701 W" and fill in with "B.R." and
model number. Consult Fan Engineering for the bias relay information.
5.4.5 Hub model comes from drawing A-4.
5.4.6 Fill in title block information as required. MWS number will be "1 ", "2", "3",
etc., per sheet numbers.
5.5 Numbers in boldface in paragraphs 5.6 through 5.18 refer to dimensions on the worksheet.
Work these numbers with the diamond dimensions on reference drawings MWS-REFI and
MWS-REF2.
5.6 Fill in motor data:
5.6.1 1,2,3,4 and rain guard number comes from drawing A-I for NEMA frame motors.
5.6.2 For non-NEMA motors, get information from catalog.
5.6.3 Non-standard rain guards have part number 52199 and bore size = shaft OD­
0.003".
5.6.4 MM, motor mount supports, and motor mount guard come from drawing A-8.
5.6.5 Put motor offset per drawing A-8 into 5, or fill in with "0" for no offset.
5.7 Fill in drive data.
5.7.1 Standard MM depth, 6, is 12", but may need to be adjusted up in 1" increments, or
to structural channel sizes, to accommodate the drive arrangement.
5.7.2 7 comes from drawing A-2.
5.7.3 8,9,10,11,12,13 are from the drive catalog or drawing A-5. Preprinted dimensions
may change with non-standard bearings or non-standard motor mount depth.
5.8 Bushing bore, 14 = 23/4" unless a bushing will not work with 2 3/4", in which case use 2
1/2".
5.9 Bearing bore, 15 & 16, is 2 15/16", standard, with a 3" shaft.
5.10 Information is preprinted for HPC 50081 upper bearing and 3000 & 1000 HPC fan hubs.
For other bearings or hubs, modify dimensions as required.
5.11 For calculating induced draft shaft length, the standard louver depth is 1'-0 and the standard
hood depth is 3'-0. Verify these numbers with the General Arrangement drawing when
available.
5.12 Fan centerline dimension, 17, is standard for 3000 & 1000 HPC fan hubs. Modify as
required for other hubs.
5.13 Fill in fan strut number: 4T** (** = fan diameter).
5.14 Fill in motor location dimensions:

STD BOOK HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION SECT. ZA - pG. 6
5.14.1 18 is calculated from motor mount standard dimensions (refer to drawing A-8).
5.14.2 Select belt guard as follows:
5.14.2.1 calculate (1/2 driven sprocket or sheave + 2 314" + 19)
5.14.2.2 round up total to next bolt spacing for belt guard from drawing A-3.
5.14.2.3 Fill in the belt guard number for standard or hinged belt guard as
required by customer specifications.
5.14.2.4 20 = bolt specification - 19. Increase 20 as required to meet the
"minimum" for 21 as printed on the MWS.
5.14.2.5 This "minimum" is a guideline for ensuring strut clearance for future
drives and may be adjusted for struts which fall just short ofthe
"minimum".
5.14.2.6 All guards are to be filled in with HPM part numbers. This may
change to HPC part numbers as required by scheduling.
5.14.3 22,23 are preprinted dimensions, but may be adjusted as required.
5.14.3.1 22 may be decreased when required for short MM lengths, but ensure
that the strut does not interfere with the drive components.
5.14.3.2 23 may be increased to comply with the requirements of 4.14.2 while
using a smaller belt guard, but care should be taken to ensure that no
access gap exists between the strut and the belt guard.
5.15 For forced draft units, fill in the fan guard dimensions and fan ring holes, 24, 25, 26, 27, 28,
29,30,31,32, per drawing A-9. All guards are to be filled in with HPM part numbers.
This may change to HPC part numbers as required by scheduling.
5.16 Fill in AV air line support picture.
5.16.1 For induced draft AV fans without fan guards and all forced draft AV fans, fill in
with "4V** & 4V02" (** = fan diameter).
5.16.2 For induced draft AV fans with fan guards, fill in with fan guard number, and
"3G02" AV support as required.
5.16.3 All guards are to be filled in with HPM part numbers. This may change to HPC
part numbers as required by scheduling (refer to drawing A-3).
5.17 Fill in notes:
5.17.1 Motor bolt diameter and foot thickness comes from drawing A-I. Grip = (5/16"
or 3/8" motor mount thickness) + foot thickness. Get bolt length from HPC
standard A307 bolt grip chart.
5.17.2 Preprinted bearing bolt dimensions are for standard bearings. For non-standard
bearings, modify as required.
5.18 For induced draft units, write in "YES" or "NO" next to "REMOVABLE FAN MOUNT:"
as required per job package.
6.0 FORCED DRAFT GEAR DRIVES
6.1 The MWS for forced draft, gear drive units is to be filled out per example document MWS­
EX3.
6.2 Numbers in boldface below refer to dimensions on the worksheet. Work these numbers
with diamond dimensions on reference drawing MWS-REF3.

6.3 Get the following information from the FFSS if available:
Job number
customer name & location (use GA if available)
PO (from job package)
customer item number(s).
number of fans
motor manufacturer, type, HP, RPM, V, PH, Hz
gear manufacturer, model, ratio
fan diameter., blade type, no. of blades, AP/AV
6.4 Select the form 'FG-AP' for AP fans, and 'FG-AV' for AV fans (refer to paragraph 1.2.1
for the location of these files). For units with both AP and AV fans, use one of each. Run
a reproducible of the selected master(s).
6.5 Fill in data along right side of form from FFSS, job package, and standards. Pay special
note to the following:
6.5.1 Standard coupling type is Rexnord DBZ-B. Other couplings may be required by
job package or customer specifications. Coupling size will be filled in later based
on the motor and gear shaft diameters.
6.5.2 Inlet bell set number comes from drawing A-3.
6.5.3 For AV fan information, valve positioner requirements come from drawing A-4.
6.5.3.1 Ifno valve positioner is required, erase "1701 WIt under "V.P.".
6.5.3.2 Ifbias relay is required per job package, erase "V.P.: 1701 WIt and fill
in with "B.R." and model no.
6.5.3.3 See Fan Engineering for bias relay information.
6.5.4 Fan hub model comes from drawing A-4. Be sure to check the gear shaft size
when this affects the hub model number and bushing.
6.5.5 Fan weight for HPC standard fans comes from drawing A-I0.
6.5.6 Fill in the title block information as required. MWS number will be "1 ", "2", "3",
etc., per sheet numbers.
6.6 Fill in motor data, including weight, from drawing A-I, or, for non-standard motors, from
the motor catalog (if 1 is unknown, leave blank).
6.7 Fill in gear data, including weight, from drawing A-II (for Amarillo gears, or from the gear
catalog (2 is gear frame + 1" approximate).
6.8 Set shims under motor/gear.
6.8.1 If3 > 4, then5 =0" and 6 =3-4.
6.8.2 If 4 > 3, then 6 = 0" and 5 = 4-3.
6.8.3 If3 = 4, then5= 6 = 0".
6.9 Size the coupling per the shaft diameters and drawing A-12 or coupling information. Be
sure to check the HP rating vs. the motor (standard coupling service factor is 2.0). Fill in
coupling dimensions.
6.10 Set motor-to-gear center distance in 1/4" increments such that 7> 8 and 9. Fill in 10,
which may be in 1/32" increments.
6.11 Fill in fan dimensions from drawing A-4, or, for non-standard fans, from other fan
information. Fill in bushing type and, for AV fans, bushing length.

STD BOOK HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION SECT. 2A -PG. 8
6.12 Fan ring depth = 2'-0 standard (2'-6 for HW & W blades or as required for other fans).
6.13 Fan location, 11 = 1'-5 (±) such that MM depth is in 1" increments (or 1/4" increments
when required), and 12 = 1". These dimensions may need to be adjusted per the following
constraints:
6.13.1 13 > 2".
6.13.2 14,15> 3" (ifpossible, 4" min. is preferred).
6.13.3 16 > 0" (or note that"guard cross bar to be spaced to clear motor").
6.13.4 1 (if known) < 16 (or note that "guard cross bar to be spaced to clear eye bolt").
6.13.5 17 3 1/4"
6.13.6 (For AV fans) 18> 3"
6.14 Calculate remaining dimensions (19 will be negative ifbase ofgear output shaft is below
the fan ring).
6.15 Fill in fan strut number,4T** and, for AV fans, AV air line support, 4V** (** = fan
diameter).
6.16 Fill in notes for motor and gear bolts. Get bolt diameter and calculate grip length from
motor and gear information. Bolt Length comes from HPC standard A307 bolt grip chart.
7.0 INDUCED DRAFT GEAR DRIVES
7.1 The MWS for induced draft, gear drive units is to be filled out per example document
MWS-EX4.
7.2 Numbers in boldface below refer to dimensions on the worksheet. Work these numbers
with diamond dimensions on reference drawing MWS-REF4.
7.3 Get the following information from the FFSS if available:
Job number
customer name & location (use GA ifavailable)
PO (from job package)
customer item number(s)
number ofbundles per unit
number of fans
motor manufacturer, type, HP, RPM, V, PH, Hz
gear manufacturer, model, ratio
fan diameter, blade type, no. of blades, AP/AV
7.4 Select the form 'NG-ST' for units with shaft-thru bundles, and 'NG-MB' for units with
multi-bundles such that the shaft extends up between two bundles (refer to paragraph 1.2.1
for the location ofthese files). Run a reproducible ofthe selected master.
7.5 Fill in data along right side ofform from FFSS, job package, and standards. Pay special
note to the following:
7.5.1 Standard motor coupling type is Rexnord DBZ-B. Standard fan shaft coupling
type is Rexnord BMR. Other couplings may be required by job package or
customer specifications. Coupling sizes will be filled in later per motor and gear
shaft diameters.
7.5.2 Inlet bell set number comes from drawing A-3.
7.5.3 For AV fan information, valve positioner requirements come from drawing A-4.

STU BOOK HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION SECT. 2A -PC. 9
7.5.4.1 Ifno valve positioner is required, erase "170IW" under "V.P."
7.5.4.2 If bias relay is required per job package, erase "V.P.: 1701 W" and fill
in with "B.R." and model number.
7.5.4.3 See Fan Engineering for bias relay information.
7.5.4 Fan hub model comes from drawing A-4. Shaft standard fan end will have a 2
7/8" taper.
7.5.5 Fan weight for HPC standard fans comes from drawing A-IO.
7.5.6 Fill in the title block information as required. MWS number will be "I ", "2", "3",
etc., per sheet numbers.
7.6 Fill in motor data, including weight, from drawing A-I, or, for non-standard motors, from
the motor catalog.
7.7 Fill in the gear data, including weight, from drawing A-II (for Amarillo gears) or from the
gear catalog.
7.8 Set shims under motor/gear.
7.8.1 If1> 2, then3 = 0" and 4 = 1-2.
7.8.2 If2> 1, then 4 = 0" and3 = 2-1.
7.8.3 If1=2, then3 =4=0".
7.9 Size the motor coupling per shaft diameters and drawing A-12 or coupling information. Be
sure to check the HP rating vs. the motor, at the motor RPM (standard coupling service
factor is 2). Fill in motor coupling dimensions.
7.10 Set motor-to-gear center distance in 1/4" increments such that 5> 6 and 7. Fill in 8, which
may be in 1/32" increments.
7.11 Size the fan shaft coupling per shaft diameters and drawing A-12 or coupling information.
Be sure to check the HP rating vs. the motor, at the fan RPM (standard coupling service
factor is 2). Standard fan shaft OD, 9, is 2 3/4" with a 5/8 x 5/16 keyway. This may be
reduced to accommodate an appropriate coupling, but not below 2". Fill in fan shaft
coupling dimensions.
7.12 Set MM Depth in 1/2" increments such that 10> 11. Fill in 12, which may be in 1/32"
increments.
7.13 Upper shaft and fan information is pre-printed for Dodge type-K bearing and 3000 & 1000
HPC fan hubs. Modify as required for other hubs or bearings.
7.14 Get the tube bundle frame depth from the GA or tube bundle frame worksheet. Get the
steam coil depth from the GA or Standards Book III. The standard louver depth is 1'-0 and
the standard hood depth is 3'-0. Verify these numbers with the GA when available.
7.15 For shaft-thru bundles, consult with Structural Engineering to size the fan mount support.
Fill in support size and depth. Ensure that the tube bundle frame depth is sufficient for the
fan mount support depth.
7.16 Calculate and fill in fan mount height, AP shaft length, and AV shaft length as appropriate.
If either an AP or an AV shaft is not required, leave the corresponding length dimension
blank. For non-standard upper or lower shaft ends, adjust shaft length accordingly.
7.17 Calculate remaining dimensions.
7.18 Fill in AV air line support picture.

STU BOOR HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION SECT. 2A -PC. 10
7.18.1 For AP fans leave blank.
7.18.2 For AV fans without fan guards, fill in with "4V** & 4V02" (** = fan diameter).
7.18.3 For AV fans with fan guards, fill in with fan guard number, and "3G02" AV
support as required.
7.18.4 All guards are to be filled in with HPM part numbers. This may change to HPC
part numbers as required by scheduling (see drawing A-3).
7.19 Fill in notes for motor and gear bolts. Get bolt diameter and calculate the grip length from
motor and gear information. Bolt Length comes from HPC standard A307 bolt grip chart.
Bearing bolts are standard for Dodge type-K bearing, modify as necessary.
8.0 REVISIONS
8.1 For revisions, Drafting modifies the original MWS.
8.2 Changes to the MWS need to be documented as a revision ifthe previous version has been
logged and issued or used to create or revise the BOM.
8.2.1 The appropriate revision block should be filled out. 'DATE' is filled out by the
checker and is the checked date. All necessary changes are noted with revision
triangles.
8.3 After revision, the MWS is checked and issued per 4.0 above. For minor revisions not
affecting the customer, the drawing may be noted as "Revision (#) not issued to customer".
For revisions not affecting Structural Engineering, the MWS does not need to be resent.
The revisions should still be maintained for documentation purposes.

I I I I
HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION
STD BOOK SECT. 28 - PG. I
MACHINERY MOUNT - DESIGNING AND DETAILING INSTRUCTIONS
1.0 PURPOSE AND INTRODUCTION
1.1 To provide designing and detailing information, as well as detailing examples for machinery
mount fabrication drawings created in both Pro Engineering (ProlE) and AutoCAD®.
1.2 To show machinery mount components in relation to each other and to other unit parts.
2.0 CONTENTS
Sections Page

2.0 CONTENTS 1

6.0 ProlENGINEER MACHINERY MOUNT DRAWING 9
7.0 AutoCAD® MACHINERY MOUNT DRA WING 16

I I I I
STD BOOK HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION SECT. 2B -PG. 2
3.0 ASSOCIATED DOCUMENTS
3.1 Job related documents
3.1.1 The following are sources for creating machinery mount drawing:
a. Visibility® Bill ofMaterial (BOM)
b. Drawing Schedule
c. Engineering Checklist
d. Mechanical Worksheet
e. General Arrangement drawing ( II-series)
f. Unit assembly drawing (1 O-series)
g. Parts List (Series Sheet)
h. Panel drawings (3-series)
i. Structural drawings (5- and 25-series)
j. Tube bundle and/or Steam Coil frame drawings (7-series)
k. Walkway drawings (8-series)
1. Shaft drawings (l01 or 102)
3.1.2 If machinery mount drawing is changed, the above documents should be checked for
changes also. Conversely, a change in any of these documents may affect the
machinery mount drawings.
3.2 HPC reference documentation
3.2.1 The following manuals are to be used for completing the Machinery Mount drawing:
HPC Standard Books: I, II-vol. I, II-vol. II, III, and IV
HPC Computer Aided Design and Drafting Standards Manual
4.0 RESPONSmn..ITIES
4.1 Drafting department will create fabrication drawing using ProlENGINEER (ProlE) or
AutoCAD program.
4.2 Detailers' responsibilities:
a. Detailing and/or revising drawing(s) per HPC standards.
b. Maintaining file management procedures, this is to include naming files according to format
and ensuring the electronic files of issued drawing is in the appropriate server folder.
c. Inquiring about input data discrepancies and design queries, making informed decisions,
and detailing accordingly. Direct questions to the assigned Section Leader, the checker(s),
or the drafting supervisor.
4.3 Checkers should check the drawing(s) against the latest reference job information and ensure
drawing clearly reflects fabrication design and instructions using standard drafting practices.
4.4 Section Leader is to review and approve drawings before releasing them for engineer's
signature and issuance to Document Control.
4.5 Engineer is to review, approve, and sign fabrication drawing, then return the drawing to
Section Leader.
4.6 Document Control receives fabrication drawing from Section Leader, distributes drawing
according to drawing schedule and distribution list upon release of the Visibility® BOM, and
files the original drawing.

5.0 MACHINERY MOUNT COMPONENTS AND CONFIGURATION OVERVIEW
5.1 The machinery mount configuration is based on the unit design, i.e., forced draft, induced draft,
belt-drive, gear-driven, removable fan mount. This section is an overview ofthe HPC standard
machinery mount assemblies with the illustrations in this section showing only general
components.
5.2 Machinery mount components common to all belt-driven designs
Side Channel • 2 - 1/4" thick press channels with 3" toed-out flanges is the HPC standard.
Machinery mountwidth is 2'-6 or3'-6(back-to-back ofside channels).
Stiffeners • 2 per machinery mount
Struts / Brace • 1 strut-@-motor required to serve as lifting angle. Struts at ends are added
when the frame extends to far beyond stiffeners. Brace is added when
distance between stiffener and strut is too great.
Fan Mount • 1 per MM required with the shaft hole centered on mount and additional
holes located according to unit design.
Holes • Slots shown as FOR SHOP USE are for jig fit-up and located at center of
fan and behind each stiffeners.
• Holes in bottom flange are for attaching belt guard.
• 2 holes are required for attaching motor mount; increase to 3 holes for
heavy-duty motor mounts.
• Grease fitting holes are placed relative to center of fan and located on both
channels.
• Hole pattern for vibration switch varies based on the switch reauired.

5.4 Induced draft, belt-driven assemblies with standard fan mount consist ofthe following
components:
Fan Mount (std) • Fan mount assembly consists of a 4" pipe, to house the shaft, with cap and
base plates welded at each end ofthe pipe.
Cap Plate • Standard hole pattern on cap plate.
Base Plate • Hole pattern on base plate is not symmetrical-about center of shaft hole.
Support Clips • One 3" x 2 1/2" x 1/4' angle clip placed at each end of side channel (total
of 4 clips per machinery mount). Clips are used for attachment to the tube
bundle frame.

5.5 Induced draft, belt drive assemblies with removable fan mount consist of the following
components:
Fan Mount • Fan mount assembly consists of one 4" pipe, two I" pipes, one tie-rod
tubing, one tie-rod bar, base plate, and a cap plate with tapered bolts
welded to its underside. Cap and base plates are welded at each end of
pipes.
Pipes • The two I" pipes are joined to the 4" pipe housing the fan shaft with two
stiffener plates. One I" pipe houses tie-rod tubing and the other I" pipe
houses a tie-rod bar.
Tie-rod Tubing • The HPC-manufactured 3/4" tubing with threaded ends serves as grease
line.
Tie-rod Bar • The purchased 3/4" bar with threaded ends serves to reinforce fan mount
assembly.
Cap Plate
• Two tapered bolts are welded to the underside of a standard cap plate and
serve as guides in the installation process.
Base Plate
• Hole pattern differs from standard base plates in that it is symmetrical
about center of shaft hole.

5.6 Forced Draft, gear-driven assemblies require the additional items.
Mount Angles • Four 5" x 5" x 1/2" angles with one pair required at motor and one pair
required at gear locations.
Supports • Angle assembly required at both ends of machinery mount and serves as
fan guard supports.
Struts • 1/4" thick pressed-channels required at both ends of machinery mount
Mounting Plate • 1/4" thick plate bolts onto mount angles and serves as the mounting
platform for both the gear and motor. A shim plate is provided to achieve
motor-to-gear alignment.
Coupling Guard • 10 GA sheet metal formed with 2 3/4" legs to cover motor and gear shaft
connection; mounted onto the mounting plate.
Strut Support • Channel, angle, and plate assembly is attached to the mount angles and the
four fan struts attach to the four slots ofthe SUDDort assemblv.
