6.0 ProlENGINEER MACHINERY MOUNT DRAWINGS
6.1 ProlE
6.1.1 ProlE designs and details the machinery mount, fan mount assembly, and tie-rod-tubing
using a Layout as the input prompt that when regenerated outputs the ProlE models and
drawing.
6.1.2 Throughout this section the generic term jOOO is used and is meant to reference the
alphanumeric job number, with an upper or lower case "j" representing any alphabet,
e.g., job number HOOO, JOOO, and so on. The generic term "4a", in upper or lower case,
attached to the job number is used and is meant to reference the 4-series drawing
identifying a particular machinery mount within the job, e.g., 4A, 4B, and so on.
6.1.3 All files and folders names must have underscores in lieu of dashes and use lowercase
lettering (i.e. jOOO_4a_ar, in lieu ofjOOO-4a-ar.); part numbers have dashes.
6.1.4 ProlE will automate the following designs:
a. Forced and induced draft belt-driven units using TB Wood's synchronous belt drives
or Gates synchronous belt or V-belt drives
b. Forced draft units with top flange holes and clips (similar to Induced draft) in lieu of
hanger holes at ends of machinery mounts or with hinged fan guard
c. Induced draft units with hanger holes at ends in lieu oftop flange holes and clips, or
with multi-bundles, or with shaft-thru machinery mount
d. Johnson designs
e. Non-standard side panel locations or thickness, bundle widths, or materials for
standard or ETO parts
f. Removable fan mounts
g. Standard motor mount
h. Machinery mounts designs using pressed or structural channel for side channels
i. Walkway hangers at rear side, far side, or at both
j. Diagonal brace with non-standard bevel
k. Vibration switches with mounting designs of four holes, three radial holes, two
holes, or one hole
6.2 The Layout consists ofsix pages.
6.2.1 The user goes through each page typing the various known parameters from an
assortment ofjob-related documents, i.e., Fin-Fan Specification Sheets, GA drawing,
Drafting Checklist, Mechanical Worksheet, etc.
6.2.2 Layout values shown in bold or italic font can be modified. All values in plain text
cannot be changed.
6.2.3 Only adjust forced draft section if forced and induced draft section if induced.
6.3 Completing ProlE Layout
6.3.1 Copy the directory G:data\pro_e_std\macb_mt\mach_mt_eto to your workspace
(i.e. on your local drive). Create a folder for all items in the job (with the name set to
whatever your job is) and put the copied folder into this job folder.
6.3.2 Change the name ofthe directory to jOOO_4a (or whatever your job and drawing letter
is) by right clicking on the folder icon, going to properties and turning off "Read Only"
for all files and folders.

6.3.3 Edit the text file 4.txt using Wordpad. Edit/Replace "job" with "JOOO" (your job no.)

the job number and drawing letter in uppercase. Save and quit.
6.3.4 Launch ProlE. Change directory to the jOOO_4a folder you just copied.

STD BOOK [SECT. 2B -PG. 13
6.4.7 After layout values are entered, open Utilitiesrrrail-Training file... and select the
4.txt file. This will run the trail file which automatically opens all files, regenerates
the assembly, renames all files from hOOO_4a to j999_4d (your job no. and dwg. letter
per paragraph 6.3.3), revises values for job and drawing letter on layout, regenerates
and saves all files, purges old versions, and ends with the drawing opened in a window.
6.5 Preparing ProlE Drawing
6.5.1 Clean up the drawing using the reference drawings in this packet. In most cases the
cleaning process will entail adjusting dimensions.
6.5.2 If a job requires standard parts to be modified, ETO versions of standard parts exist on
the server at mach_mt\mach_mt_manual-parts. These are just like standard parts,
but are set up with ETO part descriptions. To use them, copy the appropriate part to
your folder, modify the relations, part geometry, assemblies andlor drawings for your
job. These are NOT automated, but can aid in manual modifications.
6.5.3 Save the cleaned drawings.
6.6 Printing ProlE Layout and Drawing
6.6.1 Print the drawing to file using NT KIP as destination. Print the layout using NT HP
ThickA as destination, selectall sheets, and select the"..._PS" version ofyour
printer.
6.6.2 Call Document Control to confirm plotting, then open Kip Request to plot drawings.
Select Pen Table then proe_kip, select Media Type then Bond for white paper, select
ReducelEnlarge then 100% or Force Size (must use Force Size ifprint is to be folded
by machine.) Select plot file to be sent and click Submit Job button.
6.7 Give drawing and layout check prints to Section Leader.
6.8 Scrubbing check prints
6.8.1 Launch ProlE, change to same directory, open layout and enter Checker and Section
Leader's initials on page 1. (You may need to switch dims a few times to see these
parameters.) Update any incorrect data in layout. Regenerate and save (but do not close)
layout
6.8.2 Open the top assembly h999_4a.asm. Regenerate a few times to ensure update of all
layout changes. Does the model look okay? If so, open drawing. Note: it is a good idea
to only open drawings after assemblies are in session and regenerated.
6.8.3 Make the necessary changes to drawing. Note that checker and approval names have
been automatically entered into title block. Save and reprint drawing and layout. For
final print open Kip Request; for Media Type select vellum for green paper.
6.8.4 Open the top assembly h999_4a.asm. Run' ib" mapkey to create born file. Quit ProlE.
6.9 Purging files
6.9.1 After the final prints are approved, purge out old file versions and delete files that aren't
* * * *
.prt, .asm, .lay, or .drw.
6.9.2 Move h999_4a.bom file to VOLl :unixusr\boms. Set Properties: Security to "full
access".

STD BOOK HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION [SECT. 2B -PG. 14
6.9.3 Move h999_4a directory (and/or h999 directory) to G:data\production\h999. If your job
number doesn't exist yet, add it as a directory, else just put your h999_4a in the job
folder. Change all securities on directory and contents to "full access". Keep a copy of
the directory in your local drive until the next day, when the production folder has been
backed-up (back-ups are done nightly).
6.10 Revising ProlE Drawings
6.1 0.1 Copy latest version onto your local drive and make the changes using the steps listed
for scrubbing check prints, except leave out the BOM steps.
6.1 0.2 Purge out old versions and/or delete unneeded files.
6.10.3 Copy the revised version back to production, replacing the Rev. 0 versions.
6.10.4 Reset all permissions.
6.11 Modifying Existing ProlE Drawings for Use on a New Job
6.11.1 All steps are the same as above, except use the 4rename.txt trail file.
6.11.2 Replace oldjob, newjob, oldletter, and newletter per paragraph 6.3.3.
6.12 Listing of ProlE Files
6.12.1 Table 1 contains a complete listing of 4-series files, with part numbers.
6.12.2 The file path is G:data\pro_e_std\pro_hudson\indices\pro_e_indices.xls

HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION
STDBOOK SECT.2B-PG.16
7.0 AutoCAD~ MACHINERY MOUNT DRAWINGS
7.J AutoCAD~ drawings are created for the following designs:
a. Units with non-standard belt guard holes, or motor mount holes, or fan guard holes.
b. Units with old vibration switches on mounting plates welded to side-channels.
c. Units with the following non-standard components: struts, stiffeners, fan mount support
channels, motor lifting angles, walkway hangers, or induced draft mounting clips.
d. Gear-driven units.
7.2 Creating an AutoCADQI) machinery mount drawing consists of selecting an existing AutoCAD®
drawing that is most similar to the current design and modifying it to reflect the current design.
7.2.1 Select an existing AutoCAD~ drawing from the Check_ISSUED folder and save the
drawing file, changing the file name to match your current job number.
7.2.2 Change the title block information to match current FFSS and General Arrangement
drawings. Obtain drawing numbers from the drawing schedule. Add the detailer's
initials and date subsequent to checking. Add the checker's initials and date after
completing scrubbing.
7.2.3 Modify the drawing according to the Mechanical Worksheet and additional job-related
information to reflect the current job design. Modifications will certainly entail changing
dimensions and bill of material, and may entail modifying, adding, and/or deleting
details. Modifications should be in compliance with the standard and ProlE example
drawings in this procedure (AutoCAD® dimensioning will not reflect ProlE dimensions).
Modifications to the drawing BOM should be in compliance with the BOM procedures
in Standard Book I.
7.2.4 Purge drawing then save drawing.
7.3 Printing Drawing
7.3.1 Select the Print prompt then select the following parameters completing each selection
by clicking the OK button. In the Print / Plot Configuration window click on the Device
and Default Section ... and select Kip Plotter. Click on the Size button and select User
35.50 23.5. Under the Additional Parameters options select the 1imit dial. Under Plot
Preview select the F!!ll dial; review the drawing by clicking the f..review button. Make
adjustments using the Scale, Rotation, and Origin options. If satisfied with
configuration, click on the File Nqme button and §.ave the .plt file into your -Plots
folder.
7.3.2 Launch Windows Request; navigate to -Plots folder; select plot files for printing; for
Media Type: select Bond for white paper (check prints), Vellum for green paper (final
prints), for EnlargelReduce: select Force Size then click the OK button. Click the Submit
Job button after you confirm with Document Control plotter is available.
7.4 Give check prints to Section Leader.
7.5 Scrubbing Check Prints
7.5.1 Launch AutoCAD® and open the drawing.
7.5.2 Make necessary changes to drawing. Add checker and approved names into title block.
DataM AICsHIsNEuRYe MdOUNT DESIGNING AND DETAILING REV. 1,01-10-03

I L I
HUDSONPRODUCTSCORPORATION
STDBOOK ET.2B-PG.17
7.5.3 Save and print drawing. For Kip Request, select Media Type = vellum for green paper.
7.6 After final prints are approved, move the drawing file to Check_ISSUED server job folder. Keep a
copy of drawing file on your local drive until the next day, when the server folder has been backed­
up (back-ups are done nightly).
7.7 Revising AutoCAD Drawings
7.7.1 Use the steps listed in Scrubbing Check prints.
7.7.2 Copy the drawing file from the Checked_ISSUED server folder onto your local drive
then pull the current original drawing from the drawing drawer and ensure drawing
original and drawing file are the same. Write VOID on the drawing original. Check job
stick file for additional revisions
7.7.3 Change the file name of the AutoCAD drawing to latest revision number and make the
changes. Document all changes after issuance as revisions by having the latest revision
triangles placed near the revision. One revision triangle in the general vicinity of
multiple revisions is sufficient for a large number of revisions. In cases where the entire
drawing is revised, no revision triangle is needed, but clearly define the revision in the
revision comment box.
7.7.4 Initial, add revision comment, and date the revision block after completing the revisions.
Add approval initials after checking and approval of revisions.
7.7.5 Purge the drawing and print a check print for Section Leader.
7.7.6 Move drawing file into Checked_ISSUED server folder after drawing is issued for
distribution.

STD DOOK HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION SECT. 2C - PC. 1
SHAFT DRAWING
1.0 PURPOSE & INTRODUCTION
1.1 Identify responsible parties for the creation and control of shaft drawings.
1.2 Describe how to create a shaft drawing.
1.3 This work instruction should be worked with the masters. The files listed below can be
found on the Macintosh server in:
HPC-SAVOY Ethernet\CAD SERVER\*STANDARDS\SHAFT STANDARDS
1.3.1 YSHAFT-BLK MASTER (Master)
1.3.2 YSHAFT-DODGE & OTHER (Master)
1.3.3 YSHAFT-LINK (Master)
1.3.4 SHAFT EXAMPLE (Reprinted in the appendix)
2.0 CONTENTS
1.0 PURPOSE & INTRODUCTION 1
2.0 CONTENTS 1
3.0 ASSOCIATED DOCUMENTS 2
4.0 OWNERSHIP AND ISSUANCE 2
5.0 CREATION 2
6.0 REYISION 3
APPENDIX 4
SHAFT DRAWING REV. 0, 1-18-99
Data Issued
By: Barnes, Carbrey
Date: 01-09-2025, Rev: 0


============================================================
PAGE 126
============================================================

(Standard Design Manual) - Downloaded By: David Cornealius, At: 2025-12-25 14:53
*2414806-0*
I I I I
STD BOOK HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION SECT. 2C -PC. 2
3.0 ASSOCIATED DOCUMENTS
3.1 The following documents may be affected by shaft drawings.
Sheet No's
MWS
Fan Order Form
General Arrangement Drawing
Assembly Drawing
Parts List
3.2 If the shaft drawing is changed, the above documents should also be checked for changes.
Conversely, a change in any of these documents may affect the shaft drawing.
4.0 OWNERSHIP AND ISSUANCE
4.1 The shaft drawing is created, checked, and scrubbed by Drafting from masters in the master
drawing file drawer.
4.2 The checked and signed drawing is given to the Section Leader for an approval signature.
4.3 The completed shaft drawing is given to Document Control for issuance per the drawing
schedule & distribution list.
4.4 The shaft drawing will be filed by Document Control in the hanging file.
5.0 CREATION
5.1 Shaft drawings are created from one of these existing masters:
5.1.1 Dodge bearing master
5.1.2 Link-belt bearing master (HPC standard)
5.2 Ifmultiple shaft drawings are required increment the drawing number as required
5.2.1 Example: IOIAI, IOIA2, I02A3, etc.
5.3 The drawing number will vary with the type of unit.
5.3.1 Use lOlA for induced draft units.
5.3.2 Use 102A for non-standard forced draft units.
5.4 Shaft drawings are to be filled out per the sample drawing in the appendix. The drawing
number is XOOO-I01A.
5.5 Fill in the job number, client, location, PO number, bank, and customer's item number per
the job file (use the General Arrangement drawing as a reference).
5.6 The detailer's initials and date are to be filled in before checking. The checker's initials and
date are to be added after scrubbing. The Section Leader's initials and date are to be added
after review.
5.7 The following information should be taken from the mechanical worksheet.
5.7.1 Quantity: to be listed on shaft drawing per item
5.7.2 Shaft length
5.7.3 Shaft end type (fan & sheaves): depends on bearing type for V-Belts and coupling
type for Gear Drives
SHAFT DRAWING REV. 0, 1-18=99
Data Issued
By: Barnes, Carbrey
Date: 01-09-2025, Rev: 0


============================================================
PAGE 127
============================================================

(Standard Design Manual) - Downloaded By: David Cornealius, At: 2025-12-25 14:53
*2414806-0*
I I I I
STD BOOK HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION SECT. ZC -PC. 3
5.7.4 Keyway (yes or no): use no if furnished with sheaves.
5.7.5 Shaft diameter: 3" standard
5.7.6 Material specification (if different from standard): standard is "cold drawn
stressproof' A.LS.L 1144. 4140 material to be listed as 4140HT, TGP.
5.8 Shafts with different lengths and end types should carry different marks.
5.8.1 Example:
101X-l 7'-5-778
101A-2 6'-11
5.9 Identical shafts for different item(s) should carry the same mark and should be listed per
item. Draw a vertical arrow below the mark for the first item and extend it to the last item
with the same mark (see SHAFT-EXl).
5.10 Other information to be listed on the shaft drawing:
Matenal specIhcatIOns
Mill test reports
Trace-ability
5.11 For shafts with modified sheave or fan ends, add "M" to the end type mark. For non­
standard machinery mount depth, shaft end will be modified for length (see dimension on
the MWS).
5.11.1 Example: for modified end type "R" use "RM"
6.0 REVISION
6.1 The original copy in the hanging file will be modified for revisions by drafting.
6.2 Changes to the shaft drawing do not need to be documented as a revision unless the
previous version was issued.
6.3 All necessary changes are noted with revision triangles.
6.4 After revision, the shaft drawing is checked and issued per paragraph 4.0 above.
SHAFf DRAWING REV. 0, 1-18=99

I I I I
STD BOOR HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION SECT. 2D -PC. 1
FAN ORDER FORM
1.0 PURPOSE
1.1 The FOF exists as a means of ordering fans from outside manufacturers and the HPC fan
shop.
1.2 This document describes who is responsible for creating the form, how it is created, and
how the document is maintained.
2.0 CONTENTS
1.0 PURPOSE 1
2.0 CONTENTS 1
3.0 ASSOCIATED DOCUMENTS 2
4.0 OWNERSHIP AND ISSUANCE 2
5.0 CREATION 2
6.0 REVISION 3
APPENDIX 4
FAN ORDER FORM REV. 0, 1-18-99
Data Issued
By: Barnes, Carbrey
Date: 01-09-2025, Rev: 0


============================================================
PAGE 132
============================================================

(Standard Design Manual) - Downloaded By: David Cornealius, At: 2025-12-25 14:53
*2414806-0*
I I I I
STO BOOR HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION SECT. 20 -PC. 2
3.0 ASSOCIATED DOCUMENTS
3.1 The following documents may be affected by FOF changes:
Sheet numbers
Machinery Mount drawings (4 Series)
Shaft drawing
Mechanical worksheet
Coating sheet (special requirements only)
General Arrangement drawings (11 Series)
Assembly drawings (10 Series)
Parts List
3.2 If the FOF is changed, the above documents should also be checked for changes.
Conversely, a change in any ofthese documents may affect the FOF.
4.0 OWNERSHIP AND ISSUANCE
4.1 The FOF is created, checked, and scrubbed by Drafting, using the Excel master file or an
existing job.
4.2 After final printing, a hard copy of the FOF is given to the Section Leader for issuance.
4.4 A final hard copy is given to Document Control for issuance per drawing schedule &
distribution list.
4.5 The final, electronic copy is archived by Drafting (refer to the Computer Aided Design and
Drafting Standards Manual for instructions on where to save the electronic copy). The
hard copy given to Document Control will be filed in the hanging file.
5.0 CREATION
5.1 All jobs with fanes) will require a FOF.
5.2 The FOF is to be completed per the sample form, FOF-EX1 (refer to drawing A-I in the
appendix).
5.3 Enter the job number, client, location and customer's P.O. number per the job file (refer to
the General Arrangement drawings).
5.4 The detailer's initials and date are to be filled in before checking. Add the checkers initials
and date after scrubbing and before final printing.
5.5 Create a different line for each customer item number and fan type (AP or AV).
5.6 Enter quantities, fan & hub, bore size & type as required (refer to the MWS).
5.7 Enter AV fan requirements per the MWS and FFSS.
5.7.1 Valve Positioner; Moore Model 1701W (standard)
5.7.2 Bias Relay; Robert Shaw (consult Fan Engineering)
5.7.3 Split Range; consult Fan Engineering when specified.
5.7.4 Fail to Flow; all hubs fail to maximum air flow unless specified with "R" for
reverse acting which fails to minimum air flow.
5.7.4.1 Example 1105WFP should be listed as 1105WFPR.
5.7.5 Pre-load Turns; refer to Engineering Specification ES 14.12 AVfan control
recommendation.
FAN ORDER FORM REV. 0, 1":'1s;.W
Data Issued
By: Barnes, Carbrey
Date: 01-09-2025, Rev: 0


============================================================
PAGE 133
============================================================

(Standard Design Manual) - Downloaded By: David Cornealius, At: 2025-12-25 14:53
*2414806-0*
I I I I
S'I'DBuUK HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION SEC'I'.2D-PG.3
5.7.6 Degrees; refer to Engineering Specification ES 14.02 Range Spring selection
procedure 1000WAVfans (4,5 or 6 blades)
5.7.7 Color; use the chart on the bottom right hand comer ofthe FOF.
5.7.8 Item is the inventory number; use the chart on the bottom right hand comer ofthe
FOF.
5.8 Design Pitch; refer to the FFSS
5.9 Tip Speed; refer to the FFSS
5.10 Removable fan assembly; is 'yes' or 'no' (refer to the FFSS).
5.11 Do not add date under delivery date column.
5.12 Shop assembly; is 'yes' or 'no' (refer to the FFSS).
5.13 Special requirements, such as 'domestic materials', 'mill test reports', 'special material',
'special bolts', 'coating', etc., to be listed under "remarks".
5.14 For AV fans with valve positioner or bias relay, list Norgren A08-228-M3MA Filter
Regulator under "remarks". One will be required for each AV fan.
6.0 REVISION
6.1 Before making any revisions, the hard copy in the hanging file should be removed and
voided.
6.2 Drafting will retrieve the original file from archive and rename the file by adding "-R" plus
the required revision number to the name.
6.2.1 Example: G400-FOF to be renamed to G400-FOF-Rl for revision 1
6.3 Changes to the FOF do not need to be documented as a revision unless the previous version
was issued.
6.4 All necessary changes are noted with revision triangles. These exist in the Excel file
"revision triangles" in the following directory:
Q:\HPC_CAD_SERVER\HPC_CAD_DWGS\CAD_DWGS\HPC DRAFTING\SERIES SHEETS
6.5 After revision, the FOF is checked and issued per paragraph 4.0 above.
FAN ORDER F'ORM REV. 0, 1-rg.:yy

STD BOOK SECT. 2E -PG. 1
DOOR DRAWING
1.0 PURPOSE
1.1 To document infonnation for detailing and maintaining door drawings.
1.2 To illustrate the primary purpose of the door drawing: providing the door vendor with the
necessary infonnation (i.e. door sizes, quantities, hole and anchor locations and
construction specifications) for making manufacturing drawings.
2.0 CONTENTS
1.0 PURPOSE 1
2.0 CONTENTS 1
3.0 ASSOCIATED DOCUMENTS 2

I I I I
HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION
STD BOOK SECT. 2E -PG. 2
3.0 ASSOCIATED DOCUMENTS
3.1 The following documents may be affected by door changes.
FFSS
Series Sheet
Drawing Schedule
General Arrangement drawings (11 series)
Unit Assembly drawings (10 series)
Plenum Details (3 series)
Structural Drawings (5 and 25 series)
Walkway Details, e.g. floor plates (28 series)
3.2 If the doors are changed, these documents should also be checked for changes. Conversely,
a change in any ofthese documents may affect the door drawings.
4.0 OWNERSHIP AND ISSUANCE
4.1 Drafting Department
4.1.1 The detailer completes the door drawing(s) using a reproducible ofthe tracing
master unless the Section Leader instructs otherwise.
4.1.2 The Section Leader reviews and approves the drawing(s) before releasing it for an
engineering approval signature and issuance to Document Control.
4.1.3 File the computer generated drawing(s) in the appropriate location, refer to
Computer Aided Design and Drafting Standards Manual for the server location.
4.2 Engineer
4.2.1 Review the door drawing(s).
4.2.2 Discuss and resolve discrepancies with the Section Leader.
4.2.3 Sign the drawing(s) and return to the Section Leader.
4.3 Document Control
4.3.1 Receive door drawing(s) from Drafting
4.3.2 Enter the BOM into Visibility® and distribute the drawing(s) according to the
drawing schedule and distribution list.
4.3.4 File the original hard copy of the drawing(s).
5.0 REFERENCES
5.1 The following drawings can be used as references. The electronic versions can be found on
the Macintosh server in:
HPC-SAVOY Etbernet\CAD SERVER\*STANDARDS\DOOR STANDARDS

I I I I
HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION
STD BOOK SECT. 2E -PG. 3
5.1.1 2SD 1 (Door Design Arrangements) illustrates HPC door design standards and
may be used for job references.
5.1.2 2EXI (Door Detailing Example) demonstrates instructions for completing a door
drawing. The bill of material on the drawing illustrates the Visibility® BOM
configuration.
5.2 Title Block Information
5.2.1 Obtain the title block information from the FFSS and General Arrangement
drawings.
5.2.2 Obtain drawing number(s) from the drawing schedule.
5.2.3 Add the detailer's initials and drawing date prior to checking.
5.2.4 Add the checker's initials and date after scrubbing.
5.2.5 Add the original engineering approval signatures to the drawing at the first
revision stage.
6.0 REVISIONS
6.1 Detailer
6.1.1 Document all changes, after issuance, as revisions by having the latest revision
triangle placed near the revision.
6.1.2 One revision triangle in the general vicinity of several revisions is sufficient for a
high number of revisions, as directed by the Section Leader.
6.1.3 In cases where the entire drawing is revised, no revision triangle is needed, but
clearly define the revisions in the revision comment box. Again, do this as
directed by the Section Leader.
6.1.4 Check the job stick file for additional revisions before performing a revision.
6.1.5 Add original (rev 0) engineering approval signatures to title block.
6.1.6 Initial, add comments and date the revision block after completing the revisions.
6.1.7 Add the approval initials after checking and approval ofrevisions.
6.2 The Section Leader issues the drawing(s) to Document Control for distribution.
DOOR DRAWING REV. 0, 1-18-99

By: Barnes, Carbrey

STD BOOK HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION SECT. 2F -PG. 1
LOUVER DRAWING
1.0 PURPOSE
1.1 To document the work instructions for detailing and maintaining louver drawings.
1.2 To illustrate the primary purpose ofthe louver arrangement drawing which provides the
vendor with the necessary information (i.e., louver size, quantities, hole locations and
construction specifications) for making manufacturing drawings.
2.0 CONTENTS
1.0 PURPOSE 1
2.0 CONTENTS 1
3.0 ASSOCIATED DOCUMENTS 2
4.0 OWNERSHIP AND ISSUANCE 2
5.0 CREATING LOUVER DRAWINGS 3
6.0 REVISIONS 3
APPENDIX 4
LOUVER DRAWING REV. 0, 1-18-99

By: Barnes, Carbrey
Date: 01-09-2025, Rev: 0

I I I I
HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION
STD BOOK SECT. 2F -PG. 2
3.0 ASSOCIATED DOCUMENTS
3.1 the following docwnents may be affected by louver drawings.
FFSS
Parts List
Drawing Schedule
General Arrangement Drawings (11 series)
Unit Assembly Drawings (10 series)
Plenwn Details (3 series)
Structural Drawings (5 & 25 series)
Walkway Details, e.g. floor plates (28 series)
3.2 If the louvers are changed, these docwnents should also be checked for changes.
Conversely, a change in any of these docwnents may affect the louver drawing(s).
4.0 OWNERSHIP AND ISSUANCE
4.1 Drafting Detailer
4.1.1 Complete the louver drawing per paragraph 5.0 below.
4.1.2 Use the louver template in AutoCad.
4.1.3 Select a louver configuration and proceed with completing the drawing.
4.2 Section Leader
4.2.1 Check and approve drawing before releasing for engineering signature and
issuance to Docwnent Control.
4.2.2 File computer generated drawings in the appropriate location, refer to Computer
Aided Design and Drafting Standards Manual.
4.3 Engineer
4.3.1 Review the louver drawing.
4.3.2 Discuss and resolve drawing discrepancies with the Section Leader. Sign when
complete and correct.
4.3.2 Return the approved drawing to the Section Leader.
4.4 Docwnent Control
4.4.1 Receive louver drawing(s) from Drafting.
4.4.2 Upon completing the Visibility® process, distribute drawing(s) according to
drawing schedule and distribution list. The original hard copy of drawing is filed.
LOUVER DRAWING REV. 0, 1-18-99

I I I I
HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION
STDBOOK SECT.2F-PG.3
5.0 CREATING LOUVER DRAWINGS
5.1 The louver drawing standards consist of2 drawings: 9SD1 (Louver Arrangement) and
9EX1 (Louver Detailing Example). Both of these drawing standards are work instructions
and used to complete a lover drawing, along with the FFSS.
5.1.1 Drawing 9SD1illustratesHPC louverdesign standards and may be used forjob
references.
5.1.2 Example drawing 9EX1 demonstrates detailing procedures for completing a
louver drawing. The drawing BOM illustrates the description structure of louver
components and assemblies along with the Visibility® BOM configuration.
5.1.3 Electronic copies of each can be found on the Macintosh server in:
HPC-SAVOY Ethernet\CAD SERVER\*STANDARDS\LOUVER STANDARDS
5.2 Title Block Information
5.2.1 Obtain title block information from the FFSS and General Arrangement drawings.
5.2.2 Obtain drawing number(s) from the Drawing Schedule.
5.2.3 Add the detailer's initials and drawing date prior to checking.
5.2.4 Add the checker's initials and date after completing the scrubbing phase.
5.2.5 Add the original engineering approval signatures to drawing at the first revision
stage.
6.0 REVISIONS
6.1 Detailer
6.1.1 Document all changes after issuance as revisions by having the latest revision
triangle placed near the revision.
6.1.2 One revision triangle in the general vicinity of several revisions is sufficient for
large numbers of revisions.
6.1.3 In cases where the entire drawing is revised, no revision triangle is needed, but
clearly define the revision in the revision comment box.
6.1.4 Check the job stick file for additional revisions.
6.1.5 Add original (rev 0) engineering approval signatures to title block.
6.1.6 Initial, add comments and date the revision block after completing the revisions.
6.1.7 Add approval initials after checking and approving the revisions.
6.2 The Section Leader issues the drawing(s) to Document Control for distribution.
LOUVER DRAWING REV. 0, 1-18-99

By: Barnes, Carbrey
Date: 01-09-2025, Rev: 0

5.0 BOTTOM PANEL
5.1 Choosing master bottom panel (BPI, BP2, BP3, BP4)
5.1.1 Choose a master drawing for Standard Unit based on the answer to the following
equation:
«Front column centers+2)+3"-(2*bottom panel thickness»-1I8"
5.1.1.1 Use "Master Drawing BPI - Standard Unit With One Splice In Front"
if the equation result < 71 W'
5.1.1.2 Use "Master Drawing BP2 - Standard Unit With Two Splice In Front"
if the equation result> 71 W'
5.1.2 Choose a master drawing for Johnson Unit based on the answer to the following
equation:
«Front Column Centers + Column Depth)+2)+3"-(2*Bottom Panel Thickness)-1I8"
5.1.2.1 Use "Master Drawing BP3 -Johnson Unit With One Splice In Front"
ifthe equation result < 71 W'.
5.1.2.2 Use "Master Drawing BP4 -Johnson Unit With Two Splice In Front"
if the equation result> 71 W'.
5.2 Master drawing BPI - Standard unit with one splice in front.
Panel Length
5.2.1 Length for one and three fan unit: #2=((Side Column Centers + Stub Column
Depth) +2) - 1/4"
5.2.2 Length for two fan unit: #2=Center line of fan to center line of unit, - 1/4"
5.3 Panel Width
#1=(Front Column Centers+2)-1/8"
5.4 Panel Thickness
5.4.1 Material thickness = 10 GA. (1/8") (unless Drafting Check List indicates
otherwise)

NEW HOOD PROGRAM
5/31/94
• MJ.S. Group will no longer run Hood Program.
• New Hood Program runs on Macintosh only.
• See attached sheets for running Hood Program and
issuing of Hood Program sheets by Drafting Section Leader.
• Improvements made to the Hood Program
1. Lifting lugs location have been up-dated.
2. Program now handles 30 to 100 psf wind loads.
3. Fan ring standard part names have been up-dated.
• Things to look for after running the Hood Program
1. Bolts are not counted for fan guards. (When required)
2. Some problems with 3 fan common center panel hoods.
3. Need to check lifting lug size for air seal block outs. Program is set up
for W708 lifting lug. (see below for different lifting lug sizes)
4. Please check code 5 & 11 dimensions and If the two are NOT equal, then the
"Vertical Stiffener - Mark 5" Is required. Now check to see if "Mark - 5"
is listed in the Material Summary and If It is NOT listed, then make a DeN to add
"mark - 5" with the right quantity and change the quantity for "Mark - 4" as needed.
5. Non-standard lifting lug locations.
STANDARD PARTS BLOCK OUT DIMENSIONS
UFnNGLUGS A B C
W708 (3/4 X 5 1/2) 2 7/8 2 7/8 1
W709 (3/4 X 7) 3 5/8 2 7/8 1
W710 (3/4 X 8) 4 1/8 2 7/8 1
W711 (1 X 7) 3 5/8 2 7/8 1 1/4
W712 (1 X 8) 4 1/8 2 7/8 1 1/4

HOW TO RUN HOOD PROGRAM
5/31/94
Step 1: Active hypercard program: "INDUCED Hood Design"
(See below for example of hypercard Input card)
Step 2: Input data In hypercard program:
Input
Input Data Remarks
1. Job No. G999
2. Drawing No. 3A
3. Model No. Unit width from FFSS 20.5
4. Tube Lng. Input In feet 40
5. No. of rows 4
6. No. of fans 2
7. unit type NSVS
8. Hood hgt. Input In Inches 36
9. Fan dlam. Input In Inches 192
10. Wind load Select wind load (psf)30,35,40,45, 45
50,60,65,70,75,80,85,90,95,100
11. Plenum mat. code Plenum mat'l. code: 1 = 10 gao blk. 1
2 = 10 gao galv.
3 = 3/16 blk.
12. Summary copies This Is locked at 1 copy 1
13. Unit shipping code Unit shipping code - leave blank If no
spilt or enter "1" if split.
14. Drawing revision Leave blank If revision is 0
15. Unit qty. 1
16. First bundle width Inches with decimal point 120.00
17. Bundle clearance Inches with decimal point or leave blank 6.00
18. Second bundle width Inches with decimal point or leave blank 120.00
19. Bundle clearance Inches with decimal point or leave blank
20. Third bundle width Inches with decimal point or leave blank
21. Bundle clearance Inches with decimal point or leave blank
22. Fourth bundle width Inches with decimal point or leave blank
23. Unit CL to D-angle gao Inches with decimal point 234.50
24. Fan guards NS fan guard - leave blank If no
fan guards or enter "1" If 100% AP fans
or enter the percentage of AV FANS.
25. Fan ring code Fan ring code - leave blank If galvanized
or enter "1" If painted.
Step 3: Click on Hood Prog - This runs the hood program.
Step 4: Click on Print - This prints sheets 1 & 2.
(See example sheets 1 & 2 of print outs)
Step 5: Options
A. View - Used to view sheets 1 & 2.
b. Cam drawings - This will make drawing in VersaCad of
of the hole location (names: G999_3A-1_RO & G999_3A-2_RO).
Data Issued
c. Open VCAD - This opens a VersaCad drawings of the hole location.
By: Barnes, Carbredy. Utllltles- For hypercard program only. DO NOT USE.
Date: 01-09-2025, Rev: 0
